Anhui Province Will Add New County Governance 73

Four Counties Agreed to Establish Jiashan County

Mingguang Communication. The three boundaries in eastern Anhui are located at the intersection of the four counties of Chu, Lai, Gan, and Ding. Bandits are rampant, and the area is like a wasteland. The representatives of the local people, Shao Shugu and Wu Jingye, previously submitted a petition to the Civil Affairs Department of the Provincial Government of the Interior, proposing to change the administrative area and establish Jiashan County to facilitate governance. The Ministry consulted the government and the department to investigate and review. Now, the Civil Affairs Department has specially appointed Yang Hongbin to go to the four counties for detailed investigation, and convened a meeting of the county heads of the four counties in the three boundaries to discuss. It was decided that it is necessary to establish a county and divide the area for governance. A plan was drawn up to plan the five districts of Mingguang, Sanjie, Guandian, Shiba, and Zilaiqiao in Xiuyi, and the Nansanbao in the Gupeiqu District, the Lushan in the Jianxi District, the Ma Yuantang, Yingfusi, Xiaodaishan, Fanshan, Jiangninghou, and Zhang Baling districts of Chuxian, the Jiashanbao, Dabeibao, Dananbao, Panjiaying, Sanheji, and Huaixuyuan districts of Dingyuan, the Yinjiaji, Jiashanji, and Zhangpuying areas of Laian, and the old Southeast Third District of Fengyang as the territory of Jiashan County. However, due to geographical relations, Chihe, Daishan, Pancun, Ziyang, Bogang, Jiuxian, Sangji, Daijiaxiang, Jinli, and other places in the vicinity have automatically requested the Civil Affairs Department to be incorporated into the new county. It is not known how to handle it. (September 4)

The Advance of the Bandit Suppression Army in Western Anhui 74

After crossing the Yue River, they successively captured strategic locations.

The Central Government sent airplanes to bomb.

Bengbu Dispatch: Yue Shengxuan, the Commander of the Fourth Division of the Pacification of the Border Region of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and Commander of Bandit Suppression, and concurrently Commander of the 46th Division, has been directing various troops in Liu'an to cross the Pi River and suppress the Red Bandits since last month. Within a week, they have achieved consecutive victories and made rapid progress. Wang Fanqing, Brigade Commander of the 136th Brigade of the Yue Division, leading the Gao and Zhou Regiments, along with Yang Lianchi, Commander of the Liu'an Security Corps, and other units, advanced towards Xin'anji from the 27th to suppress the bandits. The Gao Regiment encountered over a thousand bandits in Meijiaji and Meijiachanggang, while the Yang Security Corps encountered over five hundred bandits in Zhajiadun and Yangliudian. Upon seeing the troops, the bandits immediately fled south. Brigade Commander Wang led his troops in pursuit. The bandits resisted stubbornly from the highlands of Gaogang Temple and Baigudun. Zhou Regiment launched a frontal feigned attack, while the Gao and Yang Regiments outflanked the bandits from both wings. After two hours of fierce fighting, the bandits were unable to withstand and fled south in disarray. At that time, there was heavy rain, so they were not pursued relentlessly. In this battle, over two hundred bandits were killed, and over thirty were captured, all of whom were executed on the spot. Brigade Commander Wang and the Security Corps then continued to search and suppress southward along the river from Xin'anji, advancing to Xinglongji and Shatandian, successively capturing strategic locations. The 342nd Regiment's 1st Battalion and various Communist Eradication Corps stationed in Liu'an County also left the city one after another, crossing the river from Shangxia Longzhua to assist in the search and suppression. They seized four Red Bandit grain depots along the way and defeated Red Bandits from Tianjialao Geng, Shatandian, and Wu's Great Alley. As a result, the bandits along the river near the city were basically eliminated. Only in the Er Tianmen area were there still a few plainclothes bandits occasionally appearing. For the sake of consolidating the rear defenses, Brigade Commander Wang did not advance rapidly for several days but camped on the beach, resting and searching for lurking bandits. They were scheduled to continue advancing towards Xujiaji from the 1st of this month. It is heard that the Central Government will send a portion of airplanes to Liu'an for reconnaissance and bombing. Each bandit suppression unit has already prepared aircraft identification flags for use when the airplanes arrive. (September 4th)

Wang Rongbao's Report on the Investigation of the Korean Incidents 75

(Continued)

The anti-Chinese riots by Koreans in Wonsan occurred on the night of July 4th. At the beginning of the incident, Vice Consul Yang telegraphed various Daotais (Circuit Intendants) and police departments of each county, requesting them to earnestly protect the lives and properties of overseas Chinese. He also notified the Chinese residents that in case of emergency, they could entrust their properties to the police and quickly flee to the Wonsan Consulate. By the 6th and 7th days, the situation became critical. Overseas Chinese inside and outside Wonsan City moved to the consulate for refuge, reaching a sudden total of one thousand people. As of the 14th, the number of people sheltered reached over two thousand three hundred. According to investigations, twenty-one Chinese residents were seriously injured due to the Korean riots. In addition, some were chased by thugs, blocked from crossing the river, and drowned. Corpses were recovered, one each in Wonsan Chuannei-ri. There are rumors of three deaths that can be confirmed and thirteen that have not yet been confirmed. Nineteen people are missing. This is the situation of the riots in Wonsan.

On the evening of July 7th at 10 p.m. in Sinuiju, Koreans rioted, gathering five to six hundred people to attack the Chinese residents of Genzacho. Fortunately, major shops had received prior notice and had already closed their doors, and only doors and windows were broken, and no goods were lost. The consulate had negotiated with the Do Governor and the police station in advance for prevention, and upon the outbreak of the riot, immediately telegraphed the police station to send a large number of police to suppress it, which quickly dispersed. All overseas Chinese went to the consulate, and all important business records of the chamber of commerce were also transported to the consulate. On the morning of the 8th, rumors worsened, and riots broke out. Many Chinese people on the road were injured. Consul Zhu, due to the urgency of the situation, rushed to the Do Office and police station to negotiate, borrowing cars to transport overseas Chinese outside the city to safety. At one point, more than one thousand two hundred people came to the consulate and chamber of commerce for refuge, and three thousand five hundred people went to Andong. Also, because the consulate and chamber of commerce buildings were small, the elderly, weak, women, and children were sent to Andong, totaling more than six hundred people. The Andong County government, the commercial port public security bureau, the general chamber of commerce, etc., designated two theaters and three cinemas to set up five shelters and properly arranged them. That night, the Sinuiju consulate and chamber of commerce were heavily guarded. Empty shops left by overseas Chinese were patrolled and guarded by the police, and there were no major losses of goods and property. An investigation the next day found fourteen people lightly injured. In addition, on the night of the 7th, rioters broke the doors, windows, glass, and wooden boards of four Chinese shops in Nakanoshima. However, the Dong Sheng Fu store suffered heavier losses, amounting to about one hundred yuan. Police officers heard the news and came out to suppress the rioters, who then turned to attack the worker dormitory of the Arakawa group outside the city, breaking in and beating worker Yu Fujing in the chest and ribs, causing his death. There were also five or six injured people. The murderers were arrested, along with others involved in the riots, totaling forty-six people detained. Also, one worker from the Sanchon Gold Mine Company in Uiju County was beaten to death by rioters. In other places, such as the Chinese residents in Seolsan, Bukchin, Daeyudong, Sonchon, Chongju, Namshi, Guseong, Yangshi, Gusan, Bakchon, Nyeongan, and Uiju, were also beaten and injured, and their shops were attacked, but the circumstances were not serious. The direct cause of this incident was that Japanese and Korean newspapers fabricated facts about the Wanbaoshan Incident and spread them widely, recklessly inciting ignorant masses in Korea. The Incheon incident, which occurred earliest, was due to an extra edition issued by the Gyeongseong Korean Daily News, which stated that in the Wanbaoshan Incident, as a result of a conflict between Chinese and Koreans, hundreds of Koreans were killed (initially saying more than two hundred, then mistakenly saying up to eight hundred), leading to public outrage and riots. As soon as our consuls in various parts of Korea received the news, they immediately requested local officials to send police to suppress the riots and requested additional armed police to be dispatched. However, during that period, the Governor-General and the Administrative Superintendent of Korea were in the process of changing over, and there was no one in charge of the Governor-General's office. Repeated requests were made, but they were unwilling to issue orders in a timely manner to mobilize arms or dispatch military police to stop the riots, resulting in inconsistent measures in various places, and the peaceful region became the scene of unprecedented massacres. No matter how the Japanese government tries to defend itself, it cannot escape its responsibility. The Korean Governor-General's office and general Japanese newspapers are still using the Wanbaoshan Incident as an excuse, claiming that Chinese oppression of Korean farmers led to this action, as if the responsibility for this Korean riot should be borne by Chinese officials, which is a distortion of the facts and is beyond reason. Therefore, in order to study where the responsibility for this incident lies, first and foremost, the truth of the Wanbaoshan Incident must be thoroughly investigated. I will now list the beginning and end of the Wanbaoshan Incident as investigated in Shenyang, summarized on the left.

1. The cause of the incident: Chinese man Hao Yongde organized the Daotian Company and rented five hundred qing of wasteland belonging to the Xiao and Zhang families in Sanxingbao for planting paddy fields. He hired Koreans to work for him, and a contract was signed and submitted to the Changchun County government for approval. The county government believed that the matter was feasible but required that the articles of association and boundary map be submitted for approval before it could be handled. It also ordered that no more than twenty Koreans should be hired. However, Hao Yongde believed that he had obtained official approval and sublet the land to nine Koreans, including Shen Lianze, and recruited more than one hundred and eighty Koreans, who immediately started digging and diverting water, destroying civilian farmland for more than twenty li, until the banks of the Yitong River. The people rose up to oppose them, preventing the Koreans from working. Japanese Consul Tashiro sent Japanese police to protect the Koreans and prevent them from stopping work. Our side also sent police to protect the Chinese. This is the origin of the negotiation.

2. The course of the negotiation: After the people of Wanbaoshan, Changchun, rose up to prevent the Korean expatriates from digging ditches and diverting water, the Koreans, backed by the power of the Japanese police, refused to stop work. At that time, Zhou Yuping, Director of the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office, initiated negotiations with Japanese Consul Tashiro. At that time, Lin, the Japanese Consul-General stationed in Liaoning, came to see Zhang, Chairman of Jilin Province, to report on this matter. Chairman Zhang had not yet received a report on this case from the Jilin Provincial Government, so he verbally agreed with Consul-General Lin that both sides would first withdraw their police before engaging in peaceful and reasoned negotiations. Lin had agreed, so Chairman Zhang ordered our side to withdraw the police, while Japan had not withdrawn and instead urged the Koreans to proceed with the ditch digging work even more urgently. Zhou Yuping conducted reasoned negotiations, arguing back and forth verbally and in writing, but to no avail.

3. The current situation on the Japanese side: The Koreans have now completed the ditch digging and water diversion, and water is already being introduced into the fields. Japanese police have occupied two civilian houses at the Majiashao entrance, erected thirty-nine military tents, hoisted the Japanese flag, and set up four machine guns. They have also dispatched three mounted police to patrol and search. Within four or five li of Majiashao, Chinese people are not allowed to walk. The current situation near Wanbaoshan is already like an area under Japanese occupation. 4. The current situation on the Chinese side: The Chinese people of Wanbaoshan once gathered to fill in the dug ditches, but Japanese police opened fire, fortunately without casualties. After our police persuaded them to stop and await negotiations, the Chinese people have all dispersed. At that time, Zhang, Chairman of Jilin, returned to Liaoning from Beiping, and Consul-General Lin also returned to Liaoning from Tokyo. After meeting, Lin was willing to study this case in detail before proceeding with negotiations. Chairman Zhang then telegraphed to summon Zhong Yu, a special commissioner for negotiations, to Liaoning, and Lin also telegraphed to summon Ishisha, the Japanese Consul in Jilin, to Liaoning, so that Zhong and Ishisha would be responsible for the negotiations. Now Zhong and Ishisha have both returned to Jilin and are scheduled to negotiate this case in Jilin or Harbin. However, Ishisha had previously attempted to mediate this matter on his own and had proposed four conditions: (1) compensation for the Koreans' losses, (2) payment of living expenses for the Koreans this year, (3) permission for the Koreans to live freely in Changchun, and (4) approval from the provincial government for the Koreans to grow rice next year. However, these four conditions have already been rejected by the provincial government. Consul-General Lin has also stated that the previously proposed conditions are all withdrawn.

According to the above, the so-called Wanbaoshan Incident is only the fact that Koreans, backed by Japanese power, oppressed the Chinese people, and there was absolutely no action by Chinese officials to oppress Korean farmers. All the propaganda in Japanese and Korean newspapers is deliberately fabricated and sensationalized. Not only do the Chinese unanimously say so, but Japanese officials also know that it is not true at all. For example, the Heihoku (Pyongan) Do Office's announcement to the Koreans stated that this kind of news is mostly unfounded. Therefore, to say that the Korean Incident and the Wanbaoshan Incident have a cause-and-effect relationship is clearly unreasonable. The key to this negotiation is that the Japanese side insists on handling everything in accordance with its domestic law, including investigations, preliminary trials, prevention of recurrence, and relief, all of which are initiated and completed by itself. Our side, on the other hand, insists on using international negotiations, including apologies, punishing the perpetrators, guaranteeing the future, and compensating for damages, all of which must be done with the consent of both parties. The point of contention here lies entirely in the issue of responsibility. Once the issue of responsibility is clarified, all of the above can be easily resolved. According to the current investigation, this responsibility lies entirely with the other side, and our side has absolutely no responsibility to speak of. There are international precedents for all negotiation methods, and the general principles are already well understood. I request that you proceed earnestly based on the established policy in order to achieve a certain victory. As for Rongbao, who has been entrusted with the mission of protecting overseas Chinese and promoting friendly relations between the two countries, such a major event has occurred within the territory of the country, resulting in the tragic death of many innocent overseas Chinese. I was unable to prevent the disaster in advance, and it has further alienated the relationship between the two countries in the future, which is contrary to my original aspirations and fills me with endless guilt. I should request that the National Government be informed and allowed to vacate my post in order to clarify my responsibility. I am extremely grateful for your understanding. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Wang Rongbao, Ambassador to Japan. (End)

Local Correspondence

Kunshan 76

The telephone company is temporarily unable to increase prices. The Kunshan Telephone Company previously hastily increased prices, which was unanimously opposed by users who refused to pay their monthly fees. The company then submitted a request to the county executive committee to maintain the original price increase plan. After deliberation by the party-government meeting, it was resolved that: (1) a price increase would only be allowed if improvements are deemed effective within ninety-two months; (2) monthly fees would be suspended if there are incidents of negligence in business. The company has already been ordered to investigate and comply.

The county government executed three kidnappers. In the case of the kidnapping of Wu Chengzhai and Wu Yunzhou in Xiemaqiao and Heshangbang, the county government sent detectives to arrest three bandits, Zhou Er Mazi, Liu A'da, and Hu Xiaoheshang. After interrogation and confirmation, they were executed by firing squad. Subsequently, the Baoshan County government arrested three accomplices, Tang Shaolian, Liu Daoai, and Yan Zhiqing. The county magistrate of this county sent police to bring the three bandits back, interrogated them separately, and all confessed to adultery, looting, and extortion. The county sentenced them to death, and the provincial government approved the sentence. At 10:00 a.m. on the 5th, County Magistrate Pang took his seat in the criminal court, signed the warrants for the three criminals, verified their identities, and tied them up to be executed by firing squad at the Shaanqian execution ground.

Qingpu 77

Chonggu Town establishes a gaslight company. Chonggu Town, which belongs to the county, has never had electric lights installed, causing inconvenience to the town. Recently, businessmen Gu Jirong, Yu Huihua, Ye Renlong, Zhu Ran, etc., collected 3,000 yuan in shares and hired technician Jin Xiangfeng to establish a gaslight company. They will install lights on a household basis, and it is expected that the project will be completed and illuminated in early October. From then on, the citizens of the town will benefit greatly.

Wuxi 78

Strictly prohibit Wuxi-Cheng auto abuse of passengers. Citizen Ji Hao stated that since the opening of the Wuxi-Cheng long-distance bus company, there have been several incidents of injuring and killing people. Recently, there has been abuse of passenger loading, and the car is bumpy and tilted when driving, which is extremely dangerous. If a major disaster occurs, the company will only be subject to criminal penalties, and that's the end of it. But who will compensate for the lives of the passengers? In order to protect the lives of passengers, I hereby petition the county government to review and approve, and promptly order the Bureau of Construction and the Bureau of Public Security to conduct a thorough inspection of the car's load capacity and construction components, stipulate passenger seats, and strictly prohibit abuse of passenger loading, so that the company will be alert. After Chen County Magistrate received the petition, he immediately instructed the Bureau of Construction to forward it to the company, instructing that passengers must be loaded according to the stipulated number of seats in the future, and abuse of loading is prohibited, subject to punishment.

The third district urgently reports robbery. Lu Shiyuan, a resident of Xu Laiqiao, Yangming Township, Third District, is currently a bookkeeper in the Ling family's lumber store outside the West Gate, and is considered well-off. At about 10 p.m. the other day, seven or eight robbers suddenly came to Lu's house, speaking in a strong northern accent, wearing dark blue short clothes, and holding weapons such as handguns, iron rulers, and flashlights. They used a large stone to break open the main gate and rushed in, immediately tying up Lu's women one by one and forcing them to reveal the location of the hidden money. Then they rummaged through chests and searched at will. After half an hour, they escaped with their stolen goods. Afterwards, an inspection of the losses revealed that clothing, decorations, cash, and other items worth more than 300 yuan were stolen.

Water police detective privately settled the case. Shao Genren, the owner of the pepper alley ferry boat near Shitangwan, Sixteenth District of the county, transported goods from Shanghai back to Wuxi the other day. When the boat docked outside the West Gate, someone secretly reported to Lu Hongtai, a detective of the Sixth Squad of the Second Water Police District, that Shao's boat had contraband hidden. Lu, based on the report, went to search with Deputy Detective You Hanwen and detective Zhou Afu, finding 25 pieces of red earth and four taels of Yuntu. They took the witness to their private residence and discussed terms, eventually settling privately for 900 yuan without bringing the team or handing over the case to the district for investigation. Now the news has leaked, and District Chief Shen is conducting a thorough investigation.

Nantong 79

The chief of the public security bureau extorted money in the name of disaster relief. After investigation and confirmation by the county party department, the county government was sent a letter to dismiss him.

The fraud case in the busy canal was thoroughly investigated by the province. The fraud case in the busy canal in Tongyi County was thoroughly investigated by the Provincial Department of Finance after being reported by the County Government. Li Baosheng, Zhu Ziruo, Chen Zhongli, and Tao Tiesheng, who were involved in the case, were escorted to the province for military law investigation. In the raid case at the new market in the south of the city, seven bandits, including Song Chaowu, were captured and sent by the Public Security Bureau to the County Government on the 5th, where they were subjected to military law investigation under the jurisdiction of the Pacification.

Fundraising methods for accommodating disaster victims. Nantong is accommodating disaster victims from Taidongxing counties in Jiangbei, which requires a large amount of money. The Jiangbei Charity Association remitted 1,000 yuan on the 5th, local wealthy people raised 15,000 yuan, and the business community raised 15,000 yuan. The Disaster Relief Association raised 30,000 yuan, which is still insufficient. County Magistrate Zhang telegraphed the Jiangbei Charity Association on the 5th, saying that the county had successively sent five Xingdong ferries and sixty boats, two thousand four hundred bags of flour, twenty thousand pieces of dry food, and one thousand pieces of medicine, but funds for the wheel and salt disaster are lacking, and it is difficult to cope. Please provide assistance quickly, etc.

The murderer surrendered himself. Lu Jin, a businessman in Qifengqiao west of the city, stabbed Gao Xiuyan to death out of jealousy. Lu fled to Shanghai and returned to Tong on the 5th to surrender himself to the court.

Jiangyin 80

The opening of the Chengxi (Jiangyin-Wuxi) road is hindered. The opening of the northern section of the Chengxi Highway was originally scheduled for the 1st of this month for the ribbon-cutting ceremony. However, there are eighteen Jiang family tombs north of the Nanha Canal Bridge. Although they were relocated during road construction, the relocation fee of 180 yuan has not yet been received, and the Construction Bureau has already closed the relocation expenses and reported them to the Finance Department for verification. The descendants of the Jiang family, due to not having the money to receive, opened a wide ditch in the middle of the highway in front of the tombs, preventing cars from passing. Negotiations are still underway, so the ribbon-cutting ceremony for the opening of the entire road is still unscheduled.

Merchants and residents of Yangshe testified that the prisoner was involved in riots. Yang's Security Corps and the Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau previously captured a bandit named Zhi Songtao and escorted him to the county for interrogation. The merchants and residents of the town, because Zhi committed riots in the town on February 6, 1928, leading the crowd to kill, set fire, and rob command, reported to the county for strict punishment. Yesterday (4th) afternoon, County Magistrate Peng summoned merchants and residents Yan Shenrun, Li Jinfan, Cai Wengui, Zhao Jinlong, Xing Aiqing, Song Guibao, Sun Jinchu, and Sun Boyuan to court to confront Zhi, proving that the shops and houses of the people were all burned under Zhi's command, and that the riots were true. Zhi claimed that he went to Shanghai in January 1928 and only admitted to participating in political work, and later served as a resident detective in Shanghai Security Office. After the interrogation, he was put in shackles and imprisoned, and the rest were ordered to return.

Nanjing 81

The Sixth Aviation Team performed a parachute jump. At 3 p.m. yesterday, the Sixth Aviation Team of the Aviation Department held a parachute jump exercise at the Capital Airport. The jumpers were He Huiwu, the leader of the team, and Huang Xiancou, a flight officer. Deputy Team Leader Huang Yuquan piloted the No. 604 Kesa aircraft. At 3 p.m., it took off from the airport. Team Leader He lay on the right lower wing, and Flight Officer Huang lay on the left lower wing. They flew around the city once on each side, then flew to their destination. At that time, the altitude was three thousand feet. The jumpers jumped down one after another, and the two parachutes fluttered in the sky, descending slowly and landing in the center of the old instructor's parade ground. The audience was extremely impressed.

Hangzhou 82

Negotiating cooperation methods between the ministry and the province for telephone lines. The Zhejiang Provincial Long-Distance Telephone Bureau had a dispute with the ministry-run long-distance telephone line due to the construction of a line to Shanghai. Negotiations lasted for half a year with no results. The Zhejiang line could not connect to Shanghai, and the line was virtually abandoned. This year, the Ministry of Transportation once sent personnel to Zhejiang to request its return. The province had to repay the construction cost of 100,000 yuan, which was still difficult to achieve. Now both sides feel that the losses are huge and intend to implement cooperation. Li Ximou, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Telephone Bureau, has formulated a method in which the Shanghai side's operating income belongs to the ministry, and the Zhejiang side's income belongs to Zhejiang, so that each gets its benefits. Li went to Beijing yesterday to discuss the matter.

Ningbo 83

The God of Wealth escaped danger, and the kidnapper drowned. Zhang A'yang, a farmer in Nanhuicun, Baiguan, Lihai, had some savings. His son was just a young man and was helping his father farm at home. Unexpectedly, twelve kidnappers suddenly came the other evening and took Zhang's son away. The villagers heard the sound and rang gongs to warn the others, and each carried guns and weapons to defend themselves. Eight bandits, seeing that the situation was not good, had already fled through Yilu Road. The remaining four bandits still held the hostage and walked along the beach. At that time, the tide was high, so the four bandits, along with the hostage, were swept away by the waves. Fortunately, the villagers who were catching the bandits had also arrived and tried their best to rescue the hostage, thus preventing the loss of life. The four bandits all drowned, and their bodies have floated up. The Shangyu County Government has sent a coroner to examine the bodies.

Hu Xiu escorted through Yong. Chen Chan, the County Magistrate of Xianju County, captured a Red Bandit named Hu Xiu in Erdu Caodian Creek last month, seizing three handguns, Red Party propaganda, and a small box of documents. It was learned that Hu was seventeen years old, a native of Yongjia, and currently serving as a certain division commander in the Red Army's First Army. On the 2nd, County Magistrate Chen, believing that Hu was an important criminal among the bandits, personally led Police Chief Li Yaoming and seven armed policemen to escort Bandit Hu to the province to be dealt with by the provincial government.

Local News

Telegraph from France: Workers Unconditionally Return to Work Today 85

Workers' Representatives Apologize

Xu A'mei Arrested Yesterday

Workers of the French Water and Electricity Company, on the 4th of this month, were connecting wires at Shenyuli, Huacheng Road, when they molested a woman and assaulted residents, leading to a conflict with the police, causing great disturbance. The French police, in order to maintain order, announced a temporary curfew for several days, and the trams were suspended for two days. Seeing the seriousness of the situation, the workers specially appointed representatives to apologize to the police and the company yesterday, and requested to return to work unconditionally today, which was understood by both organizations. Thus, the sensational disturbance came to an end. The detailed account of the events is recorded below:

▲Resolution Process: After the conflict between the workers and the French police, the workers spontaneously went on strike. Mr. Meng Suolang, the manager of the tram company, was very dissatisfied. He believed that the strike had nothing to do with the company, but the company suffered great losses. Therefore, the manager intended to hire new workers to work. Representatives of the French Water and Electricity Workers' Union, Zhang Renjun, Lu Guanhong, Ding Yougen, Qiao Linggen, and others, went to Mr. Du's residence yesterday to plead for help in restoring the workers' jobs and promised to ensure that similar incidents would not happen again in the future. At that time, Mr. Du ordered the representatives to first report to the Party Headquarters and request mediation on their behalf. After the representatives arrived at the Party Headquarters, they were lectured. Then, a representative from the Party Headquarters, Xu Yefu, along with the workers, went to Mr. Du Hua's residence and together went to the French police chief and the manager of the French Tram Company. The workers' representatives brought two apology letters and expressed their apology in person, promising to ensure that all workers would not cause similar incidents in the future. The manager said that if the workers could work peacefully and diligently, they could go to the factory to work at 11:00 tonight (i.e., last night) as usual. If they do not abide by the factory rules, they will be dismissed immediately. Furthermore, the company cannot guarantee that various administrative agencies will not arrest people at the factory in the future. The two letters are transcribed below:

▲Letter to the Company: To Whom It May Concern: Due to this unfortunate misunderstanding and conflict with the police officers, it has led to a general strike of all workers. This is truly a temporary mistake of the workers. Our representatives, in order to settle the matter and avoid the expansion of the situation, respectfully request that the Chief of Police of the Police Department allow the announcement to all workers to resume work together on Monday, and unconditionally, in addition to another apology letter to the Police Department. We specially send this letter, hoping for your understanding. Sincerely, To Mr. Manager of the French Tram Company, from representatives Zheng Deshun, Sun Heshang, Qiao Linggen, Ding Yougen, Zhang Yinsheng, Zhang Degui, Chen A'di, Zhang Sanlang, Lu Guanhong, Zhang Renjun.

▲Letter to the Police Department: To Whom It May Concern: Due to this unfortunate misunderstanding, an incident occurred involving a dispute with your police officers. This was caused by a misjudgment of the workers. Our representatives, in order to settle the matter and avoid the expansion of the situation, will be responsible for notifying all workers to resume work together on Monday. We will ensure that similar disputes will not occur in the future. We specially send this letter and express our apology. Sincerely, To Mr. Chief of Police Fervolle of your Police Department, from representatives Zheng Deshun, Sun Heshang, Qiao Linggen, Ding Yougen, Zhang Yinsheng, Zhang Degui, Chen A'di, Zhang Sanlang, Lu Guanhong, Zhang Renjun.

▲Arrest of Xu A'mei: After this disturbance occurred, the police conducted a thorough investigation and learned that Xu A'mei, an important member of the Water and Electricity Workers' Union, was present and directed everything at the time of the disturbance at the police station entrance, which was considered instigating behavior. They then reported to the Second Special Court, which issued an arrest warrant. At 3:00 PM yesterday, it was discovered that Xu was hiding in the rooftop garden of the New World Company. The head of the police immediately dispatched a reserve team and many detectives, who took police cars and first went to the Old Zha Gate Police Station to assist in the arrest. Unexpectedly, when the detectives arrived at the elevator gate, Xu was coming down the elevator, so they arrested him and took him directly to the Lujiawan General Police Station for temporary detention. At 5:00 PM, the head of the police dispatched the original detectives to Xu's residence at No. 495 Kangti Road to search the premises. They seized two large bags of various publications on the spot and transported them to the police station to await interrogation in court.

▲Receipts Seized: At 5:30 PM the day before yesterday, Peng Bowei, Inspector of the Detective Team of the Garrison Headquarters, Detectives Yang Fengqi, Xu Pengfei, and others, together with the Chief of the Second District General Office, went to the French Water and Electricity Workers' Union at No. 13 Dada Li, Luban Road, for a second search. As a result, they seized receipts from Xu A'mei for collecting three yuan per person from all workers, stating that the money was received on the 10th of this month. The Headquarters will strictly investigate the purpose of this receipt to clarify the truth.

▲Another Request for Severe Punishment: The Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai, regarding the case of Li Genfa, a fellow villager who was innocently beaten and injured by workers of the French Water and Electricity Company, convened a meeting of the executive committee to discuss countermeasures. It was decided to send a letter to the Second Court and the French Police Department, requesting them to severely punish the perpetrators according to law. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The Association believes that the Water and Electricity Company workers insulted women and beat good people, which aroused great public indignation. If the court and the police department treat this as a common injury case and leniently sentence the perpetrators, it is feared that this trend will be infinitely harmful. Therefore, they have again sent letters to the two organizations, requesting them to arrest the masterminds and severely punish them. It is hoped that the authorities of the concession will take appropriate measures to resolve the matter satisfactorily.

Yesterday's News on Disaster Relief in Various Provinces 86

Yesterday, Jiangbei Refugees Arrived in Shanghai

The China Red Swastika Society recruited more than 400 refugees in the Jiangbei area. Yesterday, they took the slow train from Zhenjiang at 1:00 PM and arrived at the North Station at 9:30 PM that night. They were transferred to Nanshi, Zhabei, and other places for resettlement.

▲News from the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters: The National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters has been very busy recently. Although yesterday was Sunday, the work of various groups continued as usual. The news from yesterday is recorded below:

▲Telegram from Tianjin: Zhu Ziqiao received a telegram from the Tianjin Flood Disaster Relief Association yesterday, stating, "Respectfully to General Zhu Ziqiao: This time, the Yangtze River Basin has been hit by floods. Our government has joined with all sectors of the Party, government, gentry, and business community in the city to organize the Tianjin Flood Disaster Relief Committee on the 27th of last month. Mayor Zhang was elected as the chairman. It was decided at the meeting to advance 60,000 yuan to Zhenyang and remit it to the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters in winter for verification and receipt. Urgent relief will be provided first. This telegram is respectfully reported. Tianjin Flood Disaster Relief Committee."

▲Telegram from Hankou: Zhu Qinglan, a member of the National Government Flood Disaster Committee, received an urgent telegram from Li Jin, the Hankou Relief Branch, yesterday, stating, "General Zhu: Received Jia Nong's telegram. Qian Kang, Cui Yang, Cha, and others have arrived. Now, after discussing with Zigon and Shaopeng, we have decided to form two teams to provide relief in the hardest-hit areas. Zigon will lead the first team to Xindi, and Shaopeng will lead the second team to Fankou. They will depart immediately. Relief supplies will be prepared and distributed by Jin. However, the disaster situation is extremely severe, and there are many victims. Please urgently raise and urge the delivery of relief supplies and funds for relief. Most urgent and hoped for. Li Jin."

▲Cheng Jingsheng's Work Report on the Disaster Area in Jiangbei: Cheng Jingsheng's report stated, "Jingsheng arrived in Zhen by night train on the 28th of last month. When passing through Su, Mr. Cao Songqiao, Yuan Xiaogu, and Hu Zuoquan, along with more than ten relief workers, boarded the train. They had already received Jingsheng's telegram. They immediately discussed relief measures on the train and did not sleep all night. At dawn, they arrived in Zhen, and Director Hu provided a car to meet them. They followed him to the provincial government to meet with Chairman Ye and Director Hu. They were filled with emotion after the reunion. Then, they met with Lu Xiaobo, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, who immediately requested that Ye and Hu hold an emergency meeting at the Chamber of Commerce. They immediately requisitioned four steamers, with sailboats attached, and carried dry food, large cakes, medicines, and the like. Secretary Li Rongzhuang and Gu Zifang were asked to escort one steamer each to Xinghua, and Jin Xingya and Yang Wanzhong were asked to escort one steamer each to Gao Shao Bao, to rescue people in different ways. Relief measures were also determined: (1) When disaster victims board the ship, their names and origins must be registered and disclosed at any time. (2) Each tugboat needs to be escorted by a relief worker, and the security team will assign soldiers to maintain order. (3) Rescued disaster victims will be sent to various resettlement areas. (4) Disaster victims who do not want to board the ship should be accommodated in thatched huts on the spot, and their food will be delivered daily by nearby shelters. (5) For remote areas where ships cannot reach, small boats should be hired to rescue and transport them to steamers. At that time, due to the shortage of relief workers, Chairman Ye was asked to assign four more people to participate in different ways: Yang Jun Dehuai, Shi Jun Zhi, Guo Jun Fuzeng, and Xu Jun Jiatang. The first to provide relief in Zhen were the Provincial Government and the Civil Affairs Department, which had dispatched commissioners with cash in advance, several thousand yuan per county, and set off by steamer. The Red Swastika Society also provided continuous relief. In addition, Yu Lengqiu and Lu Xiaobo organized the Jiangbei Temporary Righteous Relief Association, which took care of their urgent needs. This was particularly commendable. Jingsheng originally planned to depart for the disaster area with Chairman Ye the next morning, but Zhu Ziqiao's telegram arrived that day, so he did not go. Letters and telegrams were exchanged all night, and he did not sleep. The Zhenjiang resettlement centers were set up in three locations. On the 30th, four more steamers were requisitioned and dispatched to Xinghua and Dongtai. On the same day, the Jiangsu Righteous Relief Association's office in the province was established and jointly operated with the Jiangbei Temporary Righteous Association. On the same day, the Yangzhou office was also established. Cao Songqiao and Xiaogu had already gone to organize it the day before. About 500 refugees and hundreds of prisoners from Gaoyou crossed the river. President Wang of Jiangdu came to Zhen to meet with us and described the tragic situation in detail. I could not help but feel sad and cancelled dinner. Wang Yilao came to Zhen for a meeting, and the relief committee and the provincial government determined the allocation of relief funds. On the morning of the 31st, Chairman Ye and I took a steamer north and arrived in Yang at noon. We met with Songqiao and Xiaogu and learned that there were already three resettlement centers, housing more than a thousand people, providing daily meals, and the order was very good. No less than six or seven thousand people were transported to Zhen every day to seek a living on their own, which is still difficult to count. In the afternoon, we arrived at Shaobo. The water had completely receded, and the canal water had dropped by more than ten feet. Along the embankment, broken houses and dilapidated walls were everywhere. The houses on the east side of the embankment, under the embankment, were completely submerged in the water. The former densely populated settlements were completely washed away. According to the locals, the water was so fierce at that time that more than 20,000 people were washed away without a trace. The breaches along the way were more than a hundred feet wide. Mr. Wu Xiafeng said that it was really not easy to block. Chairman Ye decided to ask Brother Wang Shuxiang to discuss practical measures and ask for advice with an open mind, which is commendable for the people of Jiangbei. In the fifth village of Lujin, there were more than 3,000 refugees camping in the dense forest. The water was turbulent, and the boat could not go up, so there was no way to provide relief. I asked Chen Chuan of Jiangdu to return to Yangzhou and convey the message to Songqiao and Xiaogu to immediately requisition civilian boats and go around the lake to rescue them. The water in Gaoyou City was four or five feet deep, and all the power lines were destroyed. The prosperous streets and alleys of Sanfangli outside the North Gate were completely washed away, leaving a vast expanse of water. Floating corpses were seen far away in the treetops, undulating above the turbulent waves in the moat. Thousands of bodies were floating, and there was nowhere to bury them. The stench was nauseating. The water in the city receded six or seven feet, but in the deeper areas, it was still waist-deep. Rescue boats frequently went to and fro. The south of the city was safe and was where the disaster victims gathered. Just then, Director Li Mingyang was in You and invited Brother Shuxiang to see the breach and met with Chairman Ye. They went ashore to inspect the premises one by one. The Yunlou breach was the most dangerous. The sound of the water was surging, which was shocking. One can imagine the tragedy of the washout at that time. Everyone was in tears, and Chairman Ye was also sad and did not leave the town. That night, we stayed at the South Gate and met with Supervisor Zhang Zhijiang and Army Commander Liang Guanying. Because the water in Baoxing, Taidong, and four other counties had already forced the city to go public, and order urgently needed to be maintained, it was commendable to promise to divide the army to suppress the situation. The Huai River was not in danger, thanks to the defensive efforts of Army Commander Liang, and the various halls upstream blessed him, truly a living Buddha of all families. Shuxiang in the boat proposed temporary risk prevention to avoid expansion, and the measures are listed below. (To be continued)

Prelude to the Jiangbei Breach Closure Work 87

Ye, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, is now planning to hire Shen Zhuowu, a specialist from the Ministry of Railways, to assist in the urgent relief of the Jiangbei flood disaster. In addition to coming to Shanghai the day before yesterday to invite Zhuo Jing, Huang Keda, and American engineer Bigger, who are engineers from the American-owned Asia Construction Company of the Republic of China, to undertake the Gongjia Dike breach closure project on the Yellow River, Shen also took the night train to Zhen last night to change trains and go to the various breach sites of the Grand Canal for surveying, so that the breach closure work could be implemented as soon as possible, so that the seven counties downstream that have been flooded can plant wheat as soon as possible.

On-the-Spot Investigation of the Disaster Situation in Xinghua 88

The Xinghua Native Place Association received a letter from Zhenjiang yesterday from Mr. Liu Mingxiao, reporting on his investigation of the disaster situation after returning to Xinghua. The letter stated that Mingxiao set off on the 29th of August with the two ships hired by the provincial government, Xin Jiangshun and Xin Jiangsu, and arrived in Yangzhou in the evening. Due to the breach of the dike, the water level of the Grand Canal had receded. On the 30th, he set off from Yangzhou and entered the lower river boundary after passing through Dahanzi and Zhenwumiao. The water was turbulent and surging, forming a vast expanse of water. Only the rooftops and treetops of houses were visible along the way. The boatmen and soldiers repeatedly expressed their concerns about the extreme danger, saying that it would be extremely dangerous. On the 31st, they arrived in Xinghua and saw that only half of the higher buildings outside the city were still above the water surface. Transportation in and out of the city relied entirely on small boats. The county government hall, the junior high school, Kaiyuan Temple, and the Old Man's Mansion were not submerged, but the water level in the county government's screen wall and Gong Shengming and other places was already several inches deep. The water level in Sipailou and Dongsi Bridge was knee-deep, and the water level in Ruxue Street and West Street was chest-deep. The water level in the lower areas of the city and outside the city was shoulder-high or even covered the head. Fortunately, the market was as usual, and the order was still not chaotic. Shops and residents were living on wooden boards raised high, and although life was hard, there was no major danger. All sectors of Xinghua have now organized a temporary disaster relief association, which is located in the junior high school. The fellow villagers from Yanfu, Xintai, and the five counties of the east who traveled to Zhen organized the flood disaster relief association, which is located in the agricultural and mineral products display hall on Renzhang Road.

Urgent Telegram from County Magistrate Zhang of Taixian 89

Fan Zhengbo received an urgent telegram from County Magistrate Zhang Yi of Taixian yesterday, stating, "To Mr. Zhengbo, please forward to Xu Junlao, Wang Yilao, Huang Renlao, Huang Ronglao, Du Yueyong, Gu Zhuweng, and Wang Binweng: The You Shao Dike collapsed, and the western water flowed down, causing the upper and lower rivers of Taixian to rise together, submerging two-thirds of the entire territory. There are more than 400,000 disaster victims, who have no clothes, food, or shelter. The situation is extremely dire. Yi waded through the water and risked his life to personally supervise the police team to rescue people. He has rescued more than 20,000 disaster victims to the city in recent days, but the rest are still trapped in desperate situations. Please appeal to all parties on our behalf to quickly transport a large amount of relief food, winter clothing, and cash to Taixian to rescue the disaster. We also hope that you will send it to various newspapers and publish it in large print to spread the word. The merit will be immeasurable. Zhang Yi." Fan was shocked by the telegram and sent letters to major philanthropists, requesting them to quickly provide assistance to save the people in the disaster.

Report from Representatives of Hubei on the Real Situation in the Disaster Area 90

The Hubei Flood Disaster Relief Association's Shanghai Relief Office held a banquet at Gongdelin yesterday (the 6th) at 12:00 noon to entertain Zhu Ziqiao, Xu Jingren, and representatives of the Hubei Flood Disaster Relief Association in Shanghai, Party Committee Member Wen Juntian, Provincial Committee Member Zhu Huaibing, and High Society Representative Zhou Xingtang, and more than 30 people attended. Since the Chairman of the Office, Mr. Jiang Yuyan, had gone to Beijing and had not returned, Committee Member Liu Wanqing represented him in making inquiries. First, Mr. Zhu Ziqiao gave a speech, stating that the relief work was being presided over by Xu Jinglao in Shanghai. I had once gone to Han to observe, but I was not fully aware of the situation in various places. I hope that you can give detailed teachings on the real situation in Hubei and the process of handling relief matters, so that I can learn from them. Next, Mr. Zhu Huaibing, a member of the Hubei Provincial Government, reported on the disaster situation in Hubei. First, he described the flooding situation, stating that on July 24, the Yangtze River flooded, and the Xiang River also surged at the same time. Although attention had been paid to prevention, the disaster was unexpectedly so severe. In the past, flood prevention had been focused on the Zhanggong Dike, but this time the flooding first occurred in Danshui Pool. Within a few days, the entire city of Hankou was submerged. In Wuchang, the Xujia area had the most rapid water flow. After the Kuaizi Dike was breached, two-thirds of the city was flooded. In total, there were about 600,000 disaster victims in Wuhan. There were 45 counties in other provinces affected by the disaster, with 29 counties completely submerged, 9 counties with two-thirds submerged, and 7 counties with one-third submerged. The survey showed that there were 12 million disaster victims. Next, he talked about the relief efforts in various counties, stating that the disaster area was vast and relief was quite difficult. For emergency relief, the Emergency Relief Association first issued 5,000 yuan to each county and entrusted the county magistrates to distribute it. At the same time, they planned for follow-up work. This small amount of 5,000 yuan was really a drop in the bucket and was not enough to be called relief. However, the total amount of emergency relief from other provinces was more than 200,000 yuan. This is the real situation of the difficulty of relief. In Wuhan, fortunately, various charitable organizations and wealthy merchants have spontaneously donated money to assist the provincial government and work together. The disaster victims are not worried about starvation and are better off than the disaster victims in other counties. Next, he talked about housing. The Emergency Relief Association had the most difficulty in accommodating disaster victims. Although several shelters were set up at the time, they were soon submerged by the water. Rescuing them by boat involved countless difficulties. Whether it was using righteous ferries, restricting boat owners, or allowing them to freely demand money, it was not easy to be satisfactory. The reason was that there were so many disaster victims, who were competing for first place, and the Emergency Relief Association had limited manpower and could not be comprehensive. This cannot but be a regret. Now, several large shelters have been set up in Hanyang and Hongshan Phoenix Mountain, each of which can accommodate tens of thousands of people. However, there is a shortage of reed mats, which are not easy to purchase. They have recently been rushed from the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and Henan, which can probably be made up. Next, he talked about hygiene. In this vast flood, there was really no way to talk about hygiene. First, the drinking water was unclean. The tap water was blocked by the flood and had been cut off long ago. There was no way to do it, so they had to draw water on the spot. However, the water drawn on the spot was mixed with floating corpses, urine, and feces, and was indescribably filthy. Drinking it would easily cause diseases. Moreover, there were many mosquitoes during the flood, which also easily spread diseases. Recently, epidemics have occurred in Wuchang. Fortunately, Director Liu Ruiheng, who was sent by the central government, has established an anti-epidemic hospital, and the Emergency Relief Association has instructed all public and private hospitals to provide diagnosis and medicine free of charge, which may not be universal, but may prevent the spread. The above four points are the suffering of the disaster victims that Huaibing personally experienced in Hubei. The suffering of the disaster victims is already unbearably tragic. In addition, there are ordinary poor residents who are trapped in dangerous buildings, cut off from food and drink, with no way to call for help and no way to escape. The Emergency Relief Association has specially prepared rice, salt, oil, salted vegetables, etc., and used boats to sell or distribute them at affordable prices door to door, but it is also not easy to be universal. The disaster situation in Hubei this time is truly an unprecedented catastrophe. It is not easy to save the present, let alone the aftermath. In the blink of an eye, autumn is deep, and the cold wind is piercing the bones. Cotton clothing is a major problem for the disaster victims. Huaibing and others reported to the central government this time that they planned to use work relief and agricultural relief to seek the aftermath. Work relief will use disaster victims to repair dikes and dredge rivers, and agricultural relief will set up farmer loan offices in various counties by the Emergency Relief Association to protect arable cattle in order to restore planting. Today, the gentlemen present have repeatedly worked hard for the disaster victims in Hubei. Huaibing especially thanks on behalf of all the disaster victims in Hubei and hopes that all sectors will increase assistance. At three o'clock, they said goodbye and dispersed.

Meierhe's Report After Investigating the Yangtze River 91

Meierhe, the Inspector General of Customs, recently went to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River to investigate the disaster situation. He has now returned to Shanghai after completing his work and submitted a detailed report on the investigation results to Song, Chairman of the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Disasters. In addition to the disaster situation in various places, this report also mentions various relief issues and is very detailed. The Relief Committee will publish the most important parts of Meierhe's report as follows. According to Meierhe's report, according to past experience, if there are no special changes in the weather, the floods in Hanbu can recede to the Qi shore (45 feet 5 inches) in early October. The plains west of Hankou can recede completely within two months after mid-November. It is absolutely not true that the flood in Hanbu was caused by the breach of the Zhanggong Dike. The Zhanggong Dike was not breached. What was breached and infiltrated by water was the railway dike and the riverside road. The railway dike was very solid, but the water rose too high, exceeding the highest level in previous years by more than three feet, making it unable to support it. (According to the record, the dike was six inches higher than the highest water level in 1870, and it has been sufficient to prevent floods for more than sixty years.) Meierhe also said that if there is a lot of rain in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the river water is full early, forming a natural water gate, and at the same time, mountain floods in the upper reaches are torrential and cannot be discharged, then floods are inevitable. Fortunately, the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River flooded at the same time, which is only seen once in a hundred years. Otherwise, frequent floods would be even more unbearable. As for relief measures, Meierhe believes that dredging will definitely not work, because there is too much floating mud in the river, which cannot be removed by manual dredging. Planting trees can treat the root cause and is a long-term plan, not a symptomatic treatment. Too many dikes are also not appropriate, because the flat ground next to the dikes is too low, and sometimes it needs to be raised by alluvial mud. If only dikes are used to prevent floods, they are sufficient to prevent floods when the water is low. However, if the water continues to rise and increase, even if there is a breach, the damage will be far greater than this year. Meierhe also said that alluvial mud can make the soil fertile, and occasional overflows should be allowed to occur naturally. Finally, Meierhe also said that flood prevention should be the responsibility of a dedicated agency.

Continuing Reports of Disaster Conditions in Various Counties of Anhui 93

▲ In Fuyang, mountain torrents erupted, embankments collapsed, and the water depth on flat ground exceeded ten feet. It is estimated that over 10,000 people drowned in an area spanning 200 li north-south and 290 li east-west. Countless livestock were swept away by the massive waves. Some survivors were displaced and destitute. In mid-August, heavy snow fell for several days, with snowdrifts reaching two feet in Gaoqiu. Many more people froze to death. With no one to retrieve and bury the bodies, this is a calamity unprecedented in centuries.

Page 10

▲ In Yingshang, mountain torrents erupted, creating a vast expanse of water covering 370,000 mu. Over 20,000 houses collapsed, and reports of people and livestock being swept away by the waves continue daily. Recently, the area has also been plagued by banditry, leaving the people with no means of survival.

▲ In Huoqiu, a massive flood turned the entire county into a watery domain. All villages were destroyed, and countless livestock drowned. Over 10,000 residents were swept away by the waves. Those who survived stood forlorn in the mud, exposed to the elements, their cries echoing through the heavens, a scene too tragic to bear.

▲ In Guoyang, torrential rains caused mountain torrents, with water depths exceeding ten feet on flat ground. Boats sailed over rooftops, and countless people and livestock were swept away. This is truly a calamity unseen in a thousand years.

▲ In Mengcheng, torrential rains caused the Wo, Yi, and Fei rivers to overflow into the city, completely destroying houses. The entire county became navigable by a single reed, and countless people and livestock were swept away by the waves.

▲ In Taihe, the river overflowed, creating a vast expanse of water. A great number of houses collapsed and were submerged, and countless people and livestock drowned.

▲ In Bo County, the river overflowed, with water depths exceeding ten feet on flat ground. Fields and crops were submerged, and homes were destroyed. Many people and livestock drowned. Those without clothing or food are barely alive, a truly tragic sight.

▲ In Shou County, over ten zhang of the city wall collapsed. Only three sections of the city remained above water. Countless houses, livestock, and people were washed away. The rooftops and trees were filled with flood victims. Exposed to torrential rain, without clothing or food, the Zheng Yang Guan township was entirely submerged, with only rooftops visible.

▲ In Fengtai, ninety-six embankments successively collapsed due to the massive floods. Countless houses were destroyed, leaving 500,000 people without food or shelter, displaced and destitute, their cries shaking the earth.

▲ In Huaiyuan, the entire county was inundated, covering an area of 500,000 mu. Over 250,000 houses collapsed. The number of deaths is uncountable, and over 50,000 cattle and horses drowned. Over 400,000 people have been affected by the disaster.

▲ In Su County, hail caused damage, followed by massive flooding. Over a hundred li in all directions became a watery domain. Tens of thousands of houses collapsed. Over 300 people drowned near the city.

▲ In Fengyang, continuous rain fell for a month, causing the Huai River to flood and embankments to collapse. Both highlands and lowlands became watery domains. Fields and homes were submerged, and people and livestock were swept away. Hundreds of thousands of dying disaster victims are exposed to the elements, without food or shelter. The entire city of Linhuai Town was submerged, with only rooftops visible.

▲ In Dingyuan, both the city and rural towns became watery domains. Over 30,000 households were displaced, and over 60,000 people are without clothing or food.

▲ In Lingbi, water depths reached several feet on flat ground. Over 1,500 large and small villages were successively submerged.

A Visitor from Hunan Talks About the Disaster in Hunan 94

Wang Qi, a representative of the Hunan Provincial Government, arrived in Shanghai from Hunan. Yesterday, he told people at the Hunan Relief Association that the flooding in Hunan was more severe than in other regions. According to investigations, the most severely affected counties in Hunan this year are seven counties, including Liang, Yuanjiang, and Hanshou, which remain inundated. Following these, there are nine counties, including Xiangyin, Linxiang, and Linli. Areas such as Xinqiao, Baiguo, and Futianpu in Hengshan County, Majitang and Taohuajiang in Yiyang County, and Huashi, Jingxi, Xiabu, and the Southern Third District in Xiangtan County all span dozens of li and areas such as Chajiang, Shiziqiao, Jinximiao, Shilongkou, and Shuangjiang in Hengyang County, and Yutang, Shenchong, Heyie, and Jingshi Street in Xiangtan County all span hundreds of li, all suffering from mountain torrents. Wherever the water flowed, either the land was completely washed away, or dry land became hills. Across the aforementioned counties, the loss of grain crops is estimated to be at least over ten million mu. Other affected counties, such as Shimen, Luxi, and Yuanjiang, number thirty-three. Although the timing of the disaster varied, the total estimated loss is alarming. It is truly an unprecedented mega-flood.

The City Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop Actively Organizes Relief Efforts 95

The City Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop (50th Troop), in light of the recent flooding, has organized a Disaster Relief Service Committee, divided into Service, Fundraising, and General Affairs groups. The Service Group is dedicated to: (1) Dispatching members to local disaster relief agencies to assist in disaster area work, both indoors and outdoors, willingly accepting any task; (2) Assisting with various tasks at local disaster victim shelters, such as fire prevention and sanitation; (3) Organizing entertainment for disaster victims to alleviate their sorrow; (4) Gathering disaster-affected children to engage in various exercises and games to promote their well-being; (5) Participating in disaster relief efforts organized by the City Council or collaborating with other organizations to provide relief in disaster areas. The Fundraising Group is dedicated to: (1) Collecting funds and food donations from within and outside the troop; (2) Collecting clothing and bedding, which will be washed and repaired by troop members, sorting them into categories such as hats, shoes, clothing, pants, bedding, and other items for distribution; (3) Preparing disaster relief boxes at the Chamber of Commerce Night School, allowing the 1,000+ students to donate freely to accumulate contributions, hoping to make a significant impact; (4) Participating in large-scale fundraising events organized by the City Council. The General Affairs Group is dedicated to: document management, accounting, and publicity, working collaboratively to achieve practical results. The troop's efforts to contact various disaster relief agencies for on-site service have been well-received, with several requests already received.

The director of the association, Mr. Huang Chunzhou, personally inspected the items. Ms. Qiu Xueying personally sews any torn clothes.

▲ Suggestions on Making Biscuits to Relieve Disaster Victims. Li Jina, a secretary at the Anhui Provincial Government Secretariat, sent a letter to Zhu Ziqiao, offering suggestions on making biscuits to relieve disaster victims, stating: "When I passed Datong, I saw 200 large cakes on a lighter, shipped from Shanghai to Anhui to relieve disaster victims. They were moldy, worm-eaten, and smelled foul. I believe the biscuits were not properly baked by the biscuit workshops, and the hot weather caused them to steam and mold. The baskets they were packed in were also not sturdy, and they leaked and scattered along the way. Disaster victims who eat them will get sick. I suggest making coarse biscuits, or the best option would be to stir-fry wheat flour or rice flour until slightly yellow, add an appropriate amount of salt, and pack them in small bags made of sturdy, black paper commonly used by stores, each bag weighing one jin or two jin. Pack them in sturdy bamboo baskets and transport them to disaster areas for distribution. They do not require cooking and can be eaten with hot or cold water. They also have a salty taste, are durable, and easy to distribute. However, the amount of salt added must be carefully considered; too little will make them tasteless, and too much will make them too salty to eat. If it is difficult to get it just right, it is better to add less. The wheat flour and rice flour must be stir-fried, or they cannot be eaten with cold water. When making biscuits, someone must supervise to ensure that unsuitable items are not collected or transported. For large batches of food to be distributed for consumption, there will be malpractices if the workshop workers are perfunctory and sloppy. Supervisors must repeatedly urge and supervise, and items that do not meet the specified conditions should not only be returned but also subject to appropriate punishment to warn others." Zhu Ziqiao found Mr. Li's suggestions to be pertinent and has sent a letter to the Relief Association to consider them.

Applications to Solicit Disaster Relief Must Be Submitted First 99

New Notice from the Municipal Government

The Shanghai Municipal Government issued a notice yesterday, stating: "In order to issue a notice, the floods this year have been widespread, and the disaster situation is extremely severe. Soliciting donations and saving disaster victims is an urgent task. However, it has been reported that there have been cases of using disaster relief as a pretext to fraudulently obtain donations, which is extremely hateful. According to investigations, the supervision of temporary relief matters and charitable organizations in this city should be under the supervision of the Social Affairs Bureau. Any fundraising activities that have not been reported and registered should be banned to prevent abuses and uphold good deeds. In addition to ordering the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus to conduct strict investigations, all relief associations established in this city must first report for approval and registration to show seriousness. Those who raise funds without approval will be strictly prohibited. This order is of utmost importance."

Resolution: Appoint Committee member Tang Yingsong to review it and then submit it to the association for discussion. (9) Lawyer Jiang Shiyi is still appearing in court at all levels. Should another letter be sent to the court to prevent him? Resolution: Send a letter to courts at all levels to prevent him from appearing in court and prohibit him from establishing a law firm, and at the same time, legally recover his certificates and badges from Lawyer Jiang. (10) Member Yao Zhaodi reported that Member Gu Xianzhang introduced an unrelated person and insulted him. Resolution: Send a letter to Member Gu Xianzhang for a response. Silk Factories Gradually Resume Operations 104

Currently, There Are Over 40 Factories

The local silk industry previously suffered a sharp decline in European and American silk sales, resulting in a complete loss of capital. Factories reduced working hours and suspended machinery. After the issuance of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds, most local manufacturers, except for those who left Shanghai, have gone to the Custody Committee to collect their bonds, reaching 70-80%. However, when applying for public bonds, all manufacturers must pledge to resume operations immediately and maintain the work of female workers. Therefore, after receiving the bonds, factories are preparing to resume operations. In recent days, more than ten factories have reopened. According to the investigation, there are currently over 40 silk factories operating in Shanghai, including both old and new ones. The remaining factories are still overhauling their machinery and replenishing raw materials in preparation for resuming operations.

The township committees have been organized and officially established. Now, the county government believes that the election of village and neighborhood heads should continue immediately to complete self-governance. Therefore, County Chief Yan issued instructions to the district chiefs yesterday to supervise and urge the township chiefs to organize the election of villages and neighborhoods in order and report the progress for review.

City Chamber of Commerce Urges Filing of Business Tax Returns 106

Collection by the Wusong, Pudong, and Jiangwan Offices

Since the City Chamber of Commerce resolved to assist in collecting and paying the business tax on behalf of the government, and established a special committee and office, all investigation and reporting procedures have begun. The two letters from the Chamber of Commerce are recorded as follows:

▲ Urging the Filing of Business Returns. The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations yesterday, stating: "Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's letter stating that the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau entrusted your association to assist in collecting and paying the business tax on behalf of the government, and sent business tax return forms to be distributed to various businesses to fill out and submit to the office by August 31st, it is now September, and the aforementioned return forms have not been submitted to the office. We hereby request your association to verify and expedite the submission of filled forms to the office. For businesses, members of this association, a copy of the form is enclosed with each letter sent by this association. For other trade associations, the number of members, both members and non-members, varies. It is impossible to guess how many forms are needed. Therefore, we sent a letter to each association to collect the forms from this association's distribution office. Until recently, many people came to collect the forms, but very few filled them out and submitted them to the association. The deadline has now passed, and the Business Tax Collection Office has urged us to report quickly, making it impossible to delay any further. Therefore, we send this letter to urge all those who have not yet come to collect the return forms to verify the number of forms needed and quickly collect them from this association's distribution office. Those who have collected the forms but have not yet filled them out and submitted them to the association should fill them out according to the format. If any associations have not collected all the forms distributed to their members, they should send staff to urge them to submit them, so that they can be collected and reported by this association. All should be completed within seven days of the date of this letter."

▲ Measures for the Office to Collect Taxes. The association also sent a letter to the Wusong, Jiangwan, and Pudong offices, stipulating measures for shops in the area to collect and pay business tax. The original letter stated: "Regarding the collection of business tax in Shanghai, which is entrusted by the Finance Bureau to this association for collection and payment, this association has resolved that all industries with trade associations will be entrusted by this association to the associations for collection and payment. For shops in this city that do not have a trade association, the business tax will be collected directly by this association. The majority of shops in the three offices' areas do not have trade associations. If all shops that should pay business tax directly to this association go to this association to pay, it will be troublesome for merchants. Since the office is a branch of this association, the collection and payment of business tax in the area of the office should be entrusted to the branch offices for simplicity. Here is a copy of the notice sent to the associations on August 22nd and the collection and payment measures. After receiving this letter, each office should estimate the total number of shops in the area and the approximate number of business return forms needed, and collect them from this association's distribution office. After collecting them, distribute them to each shop to fill out and report. All should be filled out and reported within one week of the distribution of the forms."

Recent News on the Dachang Steamer Collision Case 107

Disagreement Prevents Amicable Settlement

The Navy Department States Jurisdiction Belongs to the Court

The case of the Dachang Steamer being sunk in a collision has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper due to its significant impact on the shipping industry. Both parties initially agreed to arbitration to resolve the matter. However, before arbitration could proceed, a contract needed to be established. The Shanghai Shipping Association convened three meetings with representatives from both sides, but no agreement was reached. This was because Dachang found the conditions proposed by Ping An Insurance Company to be harsh and unacceptable. The most contentious conditions are detailed below: (1) Arbitrators: Ping An insisted on a single arbitrator jointly appointed by both parties, while Dachang preferred each party to appoint one arbitrator, who would then jointly appoint a presiding arbitrator. (2) Guarantees: Ping An demanded a guarantee from Dachang, claiming it did not need to provide one itself because the ship existed. Dachang argued that arbitration conditions should be fair, with both parties providing cash guarantees or reliable commercial guarantees. (3) Scope: Ping An suggested limiting Dachang's losses to the ship's value, while Ping An’s own actual losses should be fully included. Dachang argued that the actual losses of both parties should be included, and the arbitrators should decide whether compensation was due, with no prior limitations imposed by either party. (4) Jurisdiction: Ping An insisted on designating a court, while Dachang argued that the arbitration should be final and binding, without the need for court designation. The differences between the two parties were significant, and their strong disagreements made resolution impossible. The case has been pending for months, with no arbitration in sight. Observers lamented the dispute between industry peers. Consequently, twenty fellow businesses jointly wrote to the Shipping Association, requesting the Association to arbitrate, arguing that during this period of recovering shipping rights, such arbitration should not fall into foreign hands. They pointed out that the Association's members included individuals knowledgeable in shipping and skilled in navigation, and requested the Association to convene the executive committee to select representatives to handle the case for a speedy resolution and to quell the industry dispute. Upon receiving the request, the Association sought opinions from both parties. Dachang responded favorably, but Ping An maintained its previous stance, resulting in no progress. Due to the prolonged delays and increasing losses, Dachang petitioned the Navy Department for arbitration. The Department replied that since the implementation of the Maritime Commerce Law this year, such cases fall under the jurisdiction of the judicial authorities. During court proceedings, expert witnesses are appointed to assist the trial process, and the allocation of litigation costs is also governed by regulations. The Department also instructed the pilot training institute to provide guidance within its capacity. Dachang, facing the prospect of idle crew awaiting summons and mounting debts and interest, is reportedly planning to discuss effective countermeasures with relevant parties.

Additional local news is continued on the back page.
