Local News II

Comparison of Extreme High and Low Tides 108

Highest Reached Forty-Two Feet

Since summer and autumn this year, continuous rain and frequent typhoons have led to severe flooding in various provinces, causing widespread death and injury, an unprecedented disaster. The local area has also experienced continuous rain for several days, turning rice paddies and low-lying fields into swamps. Rice plants are lying submerged in water, with unripened grains sprouting due to the water. A good autumn harvest is hopeless. The high tide has remained at a constant level throughout the day. The maximum height it reached is surely a matter of concern for the public. According to the tide gauge records kept by the Jianghai Customs House at Wusong Fort, the normal maximum water level in previous years was around thirty feet, and during large tides, it reached thirty-three to thirty-four feet. However, since the beginning of autumn this year, the normal level has already reached thirty-four feet, and large tides have reached thirty-seven feet or more, exceeding previous years by four to five feet. On the 25th of last month, during the heavy storm, the tide peaked over forty feet and remained high throughout the day. By 11 PM, it reached forty-two feet. Fortunately, the wind shifted to the northwest, and the water receded accordingly, preventing disasters between Songjiang and Shanghai. However, during the massive tide of the third day of the eighth lunar month in the 29th year of the Guangxu Emperor, the water level reached forty-three feet and five inches. That tide came unexpectedly, causing many deaths and injuries among the sandbar residents of Hengsha, Yawo Sha, Pingan Sha, and Shitou Sha. This time, casualties were also significant. Recently, during the evening tides of the past two days, the water level rose to thirty-three feet, and the daytime tides were slightly higher, but the water remained high throughout the day, receding by only one or two feet. Furthermore, this is a period of minor tides. It is feared that the tides could be even higher when major tides begin.

Misunderstanding over Missing Car 109

Schoolboy Returns Safely

A Mr. Xu, residing at No. 29 Xinzha Road, reported to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station yesterday afternoon around 4 PM that his private car, registration number 8086, and a schoolboy had suddenly disappeared, fearing a kidnapping. The police station immediately dispatched detectives to investigate. However, shortly after, the chauffeur drove the car back, and the boy was safe and sound. The commotion subsided. It is reported that Mr. Xu has three sons, all attending school. The eldest two attend a school on Jessfield Road, while the youngest attends a school on Avenue du Tonkin. Yesterday was the start of the school term, and all three boys needed to go to school. They departed together in the car around 1 PM. Before leaving, the master instructed the chauffeur to first take the youngest boy to Avenue du Tonkin and then to Jessfield Road, instructing the eldest two boys to return home in the same car. Unexpectedly, the chauffeur changed plans. After dropping off the two boys at Avenue du Tonkin, he did not go to Jessfield Road but instead took the third boy in the car for a leisurely drive on the road to pass the time. The two boys waiting at Avenue du Tonkin became anxious and returned home to inform their parents, who then reported the matter to the police station. Later, the chauffeur returned with the car, revealing the misunderstanding.

Zhen Yongfang Incites Mistress to Kill Husband 110

Pretends to Introduce Work

Luring Him to a Dark Alley to Commit the Crime

Xiao Lingbao, a Wuxi native residing at No. 40, Lane 3, Dinghe Lane, Yangshupu Road, was lured by his friend, Zhen Yongfang from Guangdong, on the pretext of introducing business, to a dark alley near the Huangpu Wharf around 11 PM on the 20th of last month. Zhen suddenly attacked Xiao with an axe, striking him on the head, causing him to fall to the ground. Xiao's wife, Zhang, who was following behind, was also injured on the head. She cried for help, and Huishan Police constables No. 859 and No. 935 rushed to the scene, apprehended Zhen, and seized the axe. They took him to the police station and sent the injured couple to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Zhen Yongfang was handed over to the Summary Court of the First Special District, awaiting Xiao's recovery for further adjudication. Now that Xiao Lingbao and his wife have recovered, the case was scheduled for further hearing yesterday. The presiding judge stated that the case should be handled by the local court, so it was transferred to the Third Criminal Court. Attorney Zhang Tianyin of the police station stated that the two parties in this case had met and become acquainted while working on a foreign steamer. The defendant often visited the plaintiff's home and initially flirted with his wife, Zhang, eventually desiring to have an affair but lacking the opportunity. In March of this year, a can of gasoline was stolen from the ship. The defendant secretly reported to the foreign foreman, accusing the plaintiff of the theft. The plaintiff was detained and sentenced to four months of imprisonment by the court. The defendant then began an affair with Zhang. On July 30th, Xiao was released from prison after serving his term. The defendant instructed Zhang to murder her husband, but she failed. Therefore, on that evening, he plotted to lure the plaintiff to that location to carry out his vicious plan. According to the two Chinese constables, they apprehended the defendant at the scene and presented the murder weapon, an axe, for inspection. Plaintiff Xiao Lingbao testified that the defendant had asked him to wait at the entrance of the first house in the alley under the pretense of introducing work. Xiao believed him and asked his wife to buy cigarettes to give to his colleagues. His wife followed behind. As soon as they arrived in the alley, the defendant suddenly attacked Xiao's head with an axe, causing him to fall to the ground and cry for help. His wife, Zhang, stated that after her husband went to prison, she had an affair with the defendant, but she still pawned her possessions to make ends meet. After her husband was released from prison, the defendant told her to murder her husband by poisoning, stabbing, or any other means, otherwise he would kill her entire family, leaving not even a rat alive. She also briefly described the defendant's actions that night. When questioned, the defendant stammered and begged for leniency. Judge Shen Bingying, after reviewing the testimony, ordered him to be remanded in custody, with a date set for sentencing.

Repercussions of Rent Increase in Baoyu Lane 113

The property in Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street, in the French Concession, belongs to Dehe Foreign Firm. The new buildings were renovated just over two years ago. Before the renovation, the rent for a single-unit building was only eighteen yuan per month. After the construction of the three-story buildings, the rent in the lane increased to sixty yuan per building. The tenants reluctantly bore the burden, fearing that they would struggle to make ends meet. The other day, they suddenly received a notice from Dehe Foreign Firm stating that from November 1st, the rent for each building would be increased to seventy-eight yuan. Upon reading the notice, the tenants were alarmed. At a time when various provinces are reporting severe droughts and commercial depression, and when rice and firewood are expensive, the landlord has suddenly increased the rent by as much as 30%, showing no consideration for business difficulties, making it difficult to accept. They have decided to convene a general meeting of tenant representatives within the next few days to discuss countermeasures and request the landlord to cancel the rent increase to ease the tenants' burden.

Female Waitress Suffers Facial Injuries 115

Improper Conduct and Reckless Affection

Former Lover Angrily Disfigures Her Face

Xu Jinbao, a woman of 39, had a romantic relationship with Lin Fengming from Vietnam, in her hometown, Jiahe. Although Lin was ten years older than Xu, she did not mind his age. They came to Shanghai together and rented a room to live together. However, life in Shanghai was extravagant, and Lin had no proper employment. Over time, they gradually struggled to make ends meet. Fortunately, Xu was still attractive, so she was introduced to work as a waitress at the Tianyun Lou in the Wing On Company. Due to the changing environment, her nature changed. Before long, rumors of her indecent behavior reached Lin's ears. Lin forced Xu to quit her job, but Xu, accustomed to a romantic lifestyle, could not bear to be restrained again. Thus, they quarreled. Lin, in extreme anger, suddenly bit Xu's face, tearing off a piece of flesh from her cheek. He then cut off the little finger and ring finger of his left hand. Later, after mediation, Xu agreed to give him thirty yuan per month, and Lin agreed not to have any further relationships with others, allowing her to continue in the same profession. Although Xu's cheek wound had healed, the scars were still visible. Unexpectedly, not long after, Lin learned that she was still behaving improperly and having reckless affairs, which he deemed unforgivable. Therefore, on the evening of the 26th of last month, he secretly brought a bottle of nitric acid and went to Tianyun Lou. Upon seeing her, he poured the acid on Xu's head to disfigure her face. After pouring the acid, he fled without a trace. In addition to reporting to the police, Xu went to the hospital for treatment. It was not until the other day that Lin was arrested by the police on Jiujiang Road. Both the victim and the suspect were sent to the First Special District Court, where presiding judge Zhou Hanting held a hearing. Police attorney Ru Baoyi stated the facts of the case, requesting that the defendant be punished under Article 294 of the Criminal Law. Xu Jinbao also recounted her relationship with the defendant and the two times she had been harmed by him. Judge Zhou then questioned the defendant and ordered him to be remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

Instigating Her to Flee with Clothes and Ornaments

Cai Xiqing, 48 years old, a merchant from Chuansha, residing at No. 803, Xinkang Lane, Jessfield Road in West Shanghai, had married a Ms. Wang through a matchmaker some years ago. After their marriage, the couple was deeply in love. However, in the first month of this year, Wang Laoer, who had recently moved in as a co-resident, secretly seduced Ms. Wang into an affair. Before long, Wang instigated her to flee with silver dollars, clothes, and ornaments. It was not until February that Cai found Wang and handed him over to the Sixth District Police Station. In the first month of this year, she was seduced by Wang Laoer, who was a co-resident, and was foolishly manipulated into fleeing with valuables and was sexually exploited. After he spent her silver dollars and pawned her clothes, she finally realized her mistake, but it was too late. She wanted to escape and return, but there was no opportunity. The defendant, Wang Laoer, 41 years old, a local resident, was charged with seducing and exploiting a married woman and defrauding her of property. The Guohua Electrical Appliances Store Case 118

Decision Pending on September 8th

The Guohua Electrical Appliances Store at No. 418 Avenue Edward VII installed a wireless radio broadcasting system to play records and tell stories to entertain the audience and expand its business. However, the International Telecommunications Office of the Ministry of Transportation discovered that it was disrupting international telecommunications frequencies. It notified the French Concession police, who dispatched officers to search Guohua and seize the broadcast equipment. The case was referred to the Second Special District Court for trial. The defendant, Zhao Xuguo, the manager of Guohua, was represented by lawyer Xuan Zhendong. The court ordered a further hearing at a later date. The hearing was held on the appointed date and was presided over by Judge Wu Fanglian in the Criminal Court. First, Police Attorney Gu Shouxi stated the facts of the case, and Xu Zhuoyun, an employee of the International Telecommunications Office, representing the plaintiff, stated that the defendant had violated telecommunications regulations and requested an investigation. The defendant's lawyer stood up and requested permission to ask the plaintiff's representative a few questions, which the court allowed. He then asked Xu whether the twenty-plus other stores in Shanghai that had installed wireless radio broadcasting systems had registered, and why they were not investigated while Guohua was. Xu replied that the others had not received orders from the Ministry. He also asked whether it was because the Guohua Wireless Radio in Suzhou had disrupted international telecommunications frequencies and this had been mistaken for the Shanghai Guohua. Xu also denied this. The defendant's lawyer then argued that Guohua's installation of wireless radio was not illegal and requested that the defendant be declared innocent. He also presented a newspaper to the court. The judge ordered the arguments to be concluded and the decision to be made on September 8th.

Claiming to Be Detectives and Extorting Silver Dollars

The Jiande Society Organizes a Charity Variety Show 120

The China Jiande Society, recognizing the severity of the floods in various provinces, organized a four-day National Flood Relief Charity Variety Show, which opened at the society's Baixing Theater at 8 PM the night before last. Society President Wang Xiaolai presided over the opening ceremony as scheduled. The chairman reported on the severity of the disasters in various regions and the process by which the society initiated the charity variety show. He stated that to help the victims, one must focus on the concept of frugality: (1) eliminate domestic warfare; (2) the government should not employ useless people; (3) individuals should be frugal; (4) families should be frugal; (5) avoid useless activities and wishful thinking. If these five points can be implemented, money can be saved and used to help the disaster victims, which will undoubtedly have a significant impact. The variety show then began, featuring various singing and dancing performances, such as Zi Luolan's "Huo Xiaoyu," Yang Naimei's "Egyptian Dance," Mei Er's "Flower Selling Song," Yang Naimei and You Guanren's "Tango Dance," Liang Saisan and Saizhu's "Butterfly Girl," Liang Saihu's "Flying Swallow Dance," and the Riyue Troupe's "Seven Emotions." Ms. Zaluolan also sang the Cantonese opera "Xiao Xiang Qin Yuan." Each session attracted over three thousand guests, demonstrating the great enthusiasm of the people of Shanghai for helping their fellow countrymen affected by the disasters. The society is scheduled to continue inviting renowned figures from Shanghai's opera world for two nights on the 12th and 13th to raise more funds and save more lives.

Reader's Correspondence

A Message from Mr. Chen Daoli

When I was eight years old, my parents had already arranged a marriage for me. At the time, I was an innocent child, so I didn't realize it. Now, as time has passed, I have become an eighteen-year-old youth. My parents now want to marry me off. Because I am currently in a period of learning and am still young and unable to support myself, I would like to postpone this matter for another three or four years. However, my parents refuse to listen to my advice. Therefore, I am helpless and am considering running away when the time comes, but I feel that this is not appropriate. Other than this, I have no other way. Therefore, I am writing to you, sir, to ask if there is any way to delay this marriage or break off this engagement, because it was arranged by the "lotus flower under the tongue" of a matchmaker. No one knows anyone's appearance or character. All I know is that she is surnamed Zhao, her father is a farmer, her mother died a few years ago, and she is a country girl who has never received an education... to avoid suffering unpleasant consequences from this "blind man riding a blind horse" marriage and regretting it later.

A Message from Mr. Yan Xuefang

Now is a civilized era, with equality between men and women and freedom of marriage. However, under this system, many young people want to divorce their spouses and marry their lovers. But in the end, they do not get good results. In recent years, I was forced by an authoritarian family to marry an illiterate woman from an old-fashioned rural family. At that time, I was studying in Beijing and had no time to oppose my family, so my parents used authoritarian means to arrange the marriage. Now that the wedding is approaching, I feel that this old-fashioned woman is not suitable to be my life partner and want to break off the engagement. However, I often have financial difficulties and cannot realize this at the moment. Moreover, her parents are unwilling to break off the engagement with me, which makes me extremely miserable. Now, I request that you, sir, provide guidance and a reply in your newspaper.

(Combined Reply to Two Messages: Both messages concern marriage contracts. This matter should be discussed from two aspects. First, from a legal perspective, Article 973 of the Civil Code states that "men under the age of seventeen and women under the age of fifteen may not enter into a marriage contract." The marriage contract entered into by Mr. Chen when he was eight years old is invalid according to the current Civil Code. However, Article 4 of the Enforcement Act makes an exception to this article. Mr. Yan says, "My parents arranged the marriage when I was in Beijing." According to Article 972 of the Civil Code, a marriage contract should be entered into by the parties themselves. If Mr. Yan's marriage was not of his own free will, it can also be considered invalid. Furthermore, according to Article 975 of the Civil Code, a marriage contract cannot be forcibly enforced. In fact, rather than forcing a marriage and causing each other lifelong suffering, it is better to break off the engagement. This is not just from a theoretical point of view, but also because it is not in line with the principle of freedom. Secondly, from a human perspective, all parents love their children. Of course, one should still carefully investigate and consider the person chosen by one's parents, but one should not think that it is definitely not possible and hurt one's parents' feelings because of this. It would be uneasy on the conscience of a child. However, we also do not advocate combining casually. For example, if the other party has not received an education, then one may as well ask them to go to school. If other issues can be remedied, one should try one's best to remedy them. When there is no other choice, one should handle it according to the law. Young people should know that the person they choose themselves may not necessarily be good. Mr. Yan said it well, "Many young people who marry their lovers do not get good results.")

A Message from Mr. Chen Rixi

I am very interested in studying social sciences, but extensive purchases are limited by economic resources. In modern schools with tight budgets, library facilities are often incomplete. A small number of books cannot satisfy my desire to read. If I travel long distances to read, it will also take up time. How can I save money and time and have the opportunity to read? I hope you, sir, can tell me.

(Reply) It is not possible for an ordinary person to buy all the books he wants to read with his own strength. Libraries are set up to solve this problem. I don't know if there are any libraries near your school that can provide you with reading materials. If there are none, or if there are not enough, there is another way. You can form a reading club in school with students in your grade or other grades who are also studying social sciences. For example, if ten people each contribute five yuan, you can buy fifty yuan worth of books. The ten people can take turns reading, or bring old books together for public reading, so it's as if you are reading fifty yuan, or even more, worth of books for the price of five yuan. You will not only save money, but also gain the benefits and joy of learning together. Do you think this method will work? A Message from Mr. Chen Songliang

After graduating from elementary school in the 17th year of the Republic [1928], my parents ordered me to enter a small money exchange as an apprentice for a term of three years, with a subsidy of 180 yuan for board and lodging. Now the term has expired and I want to change careers. Looking back on the three years, the experience I have gained is only being able to distinguish banknotes, silver dollars, and cents. I don't understand accounting at all, because the accounts of small money exchanges are all handled by the old staff, and apprentices never see them. Although I usually read bookkeeping books, the circumstances of each industry are different. Now I am in a dilemma. Please provide a solution in the newspaper.

(Reply) In addition to gaining experience in identifying currency in the small money exchange for three years, you must also be familiar with business customs and all kinds of human relationships. You are also able to pay attention to bookkeeping books on weekdays. With this kind of eager-to-learn spirit, your future is promising. It is just that you should not easily change careers. We think it is more reasonable to find a way out in the money industry. Since your apprenticeship has expired, if you can get a basic clerk position, no matter how low it is, if you can serve diligently and try to make up for or study the knowledge and skills you should have in this industry in your spare time, it will not be difficult to make progress step by step. Mr. Chen, aren't the Rong brothers, the flour kings of Wuxi, from small money exchanges? I hope you will work hard.

Communication Postage 124

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Convened a Meeting with Committee Members of All Public Associations in the City 125

Held at 2 PM Today in the Grand Auditorium of the Chamber

Since the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce organized the Committee for Inspecting Japanese Goods, it has been working very hard. In order to thoroughly boycott Japanese goods, it organized inspection teams for each industry, with the chairman of each industry as the director of the team and the executive committee members as members. The inspection work will begin throughout the city before the 10th of this month. A discussion will be held at 2 PM today in the Grand Auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, convening the chairmen and executive committee members of all industry associations in the city to discuss inspection policies and long-term measures.

The Anti-Japanese Design Association Holds its Sixth Meeting Today 126

Since its establishment, the Anti-Japanese Design Association has submitted for approval and implementation various important cases, such as setting up sugar factories and reducing national coal transportation costs. It is reported that the association is scheduled to hold its sixth committee meeting today (Monday) at 5 PM in the standing committee room of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited Mr. Li Wenjie, a standing committee member of the association, and Mr. Xue Guangqian, the secretary, to inquire about everything. According to them, there are three major resolutions in the sixth meeting that need to be seriously discussed: (1) Whether to change the method of disposing of Japanese goods and find other appropriate means of transportation; (2) To study Mr. Que Pingzhi's proposal to urge industrial factories to step up production; (3) To discuss the proposal of the cotton cloth industry to classify cotton cloth made by Japanese merchants in Shanghai factories as necessities and raw cotton embryos as raw materials, and pay industrial funds in accordance with the regulations for raw materials and necessities to supervise the establishment of factories. The Five-Year Industrial Plan was previously reported by three gentlemen including Ji Yanfang. Due to the importance of the matter, it could not be drafted, but according to Mr. Li and Mr. Xue, it still needs to be submitted to the meeting for careful decision.

The gathering ended joyfully at around 9 PM.

Xu Longxiang Flower Clothing Factory Careless 129

Still Not Extinguished as of This Morning

The Xu Longxiang Flower Clothing Factory at No. 1137 Chang'an Road, Guangzhao Road, Zhabei, suddenly caught fire at 11:30 last night. The fire burst through the roof, and the No. 1 warehouse, which was full of flower clothing, was completely burned. It was still not extinguished as of 2 AM this morning, and the loss was very heavy.

Tricked into Believing She Was a Mistress's Sister, He is Fooled 130

The Wife Acts as a Matchmaker for Her Husband

The Older Sister Arranges the Marriage for Her Younger Sister

Gao Jiansheng, who lives in Zhujiatang, Toutu, 28th Bao, South End of Hongqiao Town, West Shanghai, is nearly forty years old. His wife, Ms. Li, has not had any children. Gao Jiansheng is saddened by the lack of offspring and has long planned to take a concubine to continue the family line, but it has been difficult to find one for a while. However, Ms. Li has a younger sister (born of the same mother but a different father), named Lin Bao, who is graceful, beautiful, and intelligent, and is just twenty years old and not yet engaged. Gao Jiansheng obtained Ms. Li's consent and wanted to marry Lin Bao as a concubine. His wife, Ms. Li, was also willing to act as a matchmaker for her husband and make it a beautiful thing, but she was afraid that her mother would not agree. Therefore, Ms. Li tried to arrange it. Lin Bao was young and ignorant, with a weak will, and was also persuaded and enticed by her sister. Gao Jiansheng forcibly raped her, and it happened more than once. Recently, because she was secretly pregnant and her belly was gradually growing, her mother, Ms. Li Yu, discovered it. She severely questioned her daughter again and again, and finally, she told the truth. Her mother was furious and severely scolded her. Lin Bao then realized that she had been deceived by her sister, and her reputation was ruined. She was so heartbroken that she wanted to commit suicide several times, but she was rescued. It is now reported that Ms. Li Yu and Li Linbao, mother and daughter, have sued their son-in-law in the District Court for rape. The trial will be held soon.

Robbers of Changxing Cigarette Paper Shop Arrested 131

The Injured Shop Assistant Has Not Escaped Danger

The Changxing Cigarette Paper Shop at No. 91, Lanweiai Road (i.e., opposite the Second District Headquarters of Tangjiawan), was robbed unsuccessfully the day before yesterday (the 4th). The shop assistant, Gao Ronghua, blew the police whistle wildly and was shot and wounded by the robbers. He was taken to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, as previously reported. It is now reported that the shop assistant, Gao Ronghua, was shot in the waist, and the bullet did not come out. Yesterday, after the hospital doctor examined him, he broke open Gao's abdomen and removed the bullet, and stitched up the wound. According to the doctor, if there are no changes in three days, his life can be saved. After the police station received the report of the case, Detective Jin Jiulin of the Robbery Case Squad went to the shop to investigate and inquired in detail about the appearance, clothing, and accents of the robbers. Yesterday, Detective Jin learned that the robbers were hiding in a small inn in Tangjiawan. He immediately led detectives to the place and arrested the four robbers involved in the case. They were taken back to the police station for detention, and the apprentices and shop assistants of the shop were ordered to go to identify them, which was confirmed to be correct. They will be sent to the court for interrogation.

The Three-Route Public Buses Suspended 132

The Zhabei Huashang Three-Route Public Buses, which run between the North Railway Station and Zhenru, have been suspended since yesterday due to the continuous heavy rain and muddy roads. They will be announced to resume operation as soon as the weather clears.

The Star's New Film "Shadow of Red Tears" Premieres 133

At 12 o'clock the night before last, the Star Film Company premiered its new film "Shadow of Red Tears" at the Central Grand Theater. This film is a masterpiece by the famous director Zheng Zhengqiu. Director, screenwriter, and explanation are all done by Mr. Zheng himself. The film is 20 volumes long and divided into two parts. The idea is novel, containing sweetness, fragrance, love, tenderness, sadness, and stimulation in one furnace, and is indeed a precious work. The film's scenery was designed and created by the assistant director Cai Chusheng, and it is magnificent and unprecedented. Hu Die plays Hong'er with gentleness, without losing the style of a great lady. Xia Peizhen plays Ai Lian, who is lively and flippant, just right. Zheng Xiaoqiu plays Xi Yili, a young man who is heroic and wise, and his performance is impeccable. As for Gong Jianong's An Haobo, Xiao Ying's Xi's father, Zhao Jingxia's Dai's mother, and Huang Junfu's servant, they can all express their personalities and are just right. Overall, the entire drama has many highlights. The opening date is near, and it will surely be a sensation for a while.

The Hubei Flood Relief Emergency Relief Office in Shanghai is actively raising relief funds to be remitted to Wuhan for relief, as the disaster situation in Hubei Province is extremely serious. Yesterday, Mr. Tian Jiwei, a Hubei native in Shanghai, initiated the organization of soliciting calligraphy and paintings to help disaster relief, and invited famous calligraphers and painters in Shanghai, Xu Jingren, Yu Youren, Shen Xinhai, Cheng Yaosheng, Shang Shengbai, Chu Litang, Huang Binhong, Wang Zhongshan, Dong Shuxiong, Song Quan, Ma Qizhou, Hong Lisheng, Sun Xueni, He Tianjian, and Wang Yingbin to join the initiators. In addition to donating fine calligraphy, paintings, and works from their collections, they also advertised to solicit new and old calligraphy and paintings from collectors, literati, and elegant scholars at home and abroad, hoping to create a grand exhibition. All proceeds from the sale will be remitted to Wuhan to save the people affected by the disaster.

The Improvement of Pathé Records 136

Since the Pathé Company on Sichuan Road was acquired by British merchants, it has spared no expense in improving and renovating various facilities and the sound recording and manufacturing of records. The novelty of all the machines and the excellence of the engineering technicians are sufficient to make the products exquisite. The records previously released by the company all had red paper trademarks. Now, the old wax cylinders have been improved, and the manufactured records are better than before. The trademark on the records has been specially changed to blue paper to distinguish them. As for the films recently produced using the latest electrical sound recording method, they are affixed with black paper trademarks.

It was resolved that the fundraisers be promoted to lead the parade and solicit donations within the scope of Beisichuan Road to Si Kao Tuo Road and Disiwei Road in this area, in order to help the disaster victims. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Weather Report 143

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, stating that the weather here along the coast is overcast and foggy, with possible drizzle. The Shandong coast and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy. The wind north of Ma'an Island is gentle and non-directional. There is an easterly wind in the south. The hurricane continues to move slowly northwestward and will reach southeast of Miyako Island. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 73.9 and the lowest was 69.3. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 83.5 and the lowest was 73.8.

Ministry of Education Commends Jiang Dejun for Donating Funds to Support Education 144

Donating 33,800 Yuan

The Ministry of Education instructed the Hunan Provincial Department of Education: Upon investigation, Jiang Dejun, a citizen of Xiangxiang County, Hunan Province, has donated funds to support education, amounting to more than 30,000 yuan. After verification, the facts are confirmed. According to the regulations on commendation for donating funds to support education, he should be awarded a first-class certificate of merit. In addition to publishing the information in the Ministry's gazette for publicity and submitting it to the Ministry for commendation at the end of the year, a first-class certificate of merit should be issued. You are hereby instructed to forward it.

Reorganization of the Russian and Art Colleges in Beiping 146

The Ministry of Education had previously ordered the Beiping Russian Language and Political Science College and the Art College to be closed down gradually each year. After the Russian Language and Political Science College was closed, the Ministry of Education ordered Peking University to transform the college into a business school affiliated with Peking University, in order to cultivate Russian language specialists. To adapt to local conditions, the curriculum of the business school should focus on the study of Sino-Russian economic relations. A Russian language class should be specially established within the Peking University Affiliated Senior High School, and first-year students should be recruited during this summer vacation to prepare for further studies after the establishment of the business school. After the Art College is closed, the Ministry of Education will reorganize it into the National Beiping Art Vocational School based on the original foundation of the college, in accordance with the regulations on the organization of vocational schools.

Local News

Re-election Meeting of the Municipal Boy Scout Council 147

Held at the Municipal Education Bureau Yesterday Afternoon

The Shanghai Municipal Boy Scout Council of China held its first city-wide service personnel election meeting at the Municipal Education Bureau at 1:00 PM yesterday. Details are as follows:

▲ Meeting Staff: Presidium: Tong Xingbai, Xu Peihuang, Gu Zhengli; Master of Ceremonies: Wang Wenhua; Recorder: Luo Lie; Discipline: 196th Group (Liangjiang Girl Scouts)

▲ Meeting Order: 1. Opening; 2. Stand at attention; 3. Sing the Party song; 4. Bow to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Premier; 5. Read the Premier's will respectfully; 6. Silent tribute; 7. Chairman's report; 8. Report on the work of the Municipal Boy Scout Council over the past year; 9. Speech by the representative of the China Boy Scout Headquarters; 10. Speech by the representative of the Municipal Party Committee; 11. Speech by the representative of the Municipal Government; 12. Speech by the representative of the Municipal Education Bureau; 13. Election; 14. Vote Counting; 15. Adjournment

▲ Number of Attendees: Representatives and election supervisors from the China Boy Scout Headquarters, Tong Xingbai; representative from the Municipal Party Committee, Zhu Jiarang; representative from the Municipal Government, Chen Kecheng; representative from the Municipal Education Bureau, Zhou Shang; and over a hundred city-wide service personnel.

▲ Chairman's Report: Chairman Gu Zhengli reported, stating that he had recently traveled to Japan to inspect Boy Scout activities and lectured in Beiping for a considerable amount of time, so he was not very familiar with the recent Boy Scout situation in Shanghai. He felt ashamed that he was unable to give a comprehensive report, but he hoped everyone would understand. The number of attendees has reached the legal quorum, so he declared the grand meeting open.

▲ Representatives' Speeches: Representative of the China Boy Scout Headquarters, Tong Xingbai, stated that he was sent by the Boy Scout Headquarters to attend the election supervision and offer a few words for reference. Although the Boy Scout cause is led by both the Party and the government, the Boy Scout community itself must work hard to achieve success. In the past, the Boy Scouts in this city lacked a sound organization, making it difficult to develop. Therefore, the Party and the government had to take charge and find ways to support it. Now that the Council has been established and the Boy Scouts in this city have a central organization, the selection of council members is done by the Boy Scout community, not appointed by the Party and the government. This shows that the entire responsibility of the Boy Scout cause is being gradually handed over to you. The Party and the government are only providing support. As your responsibilities are greater than before, you should work harder to ensure a sound organization and a great strength, so that the Boy Scout cause in this city can make significant progress. In terms of the election, the Headquarters has clearly stated on the ballot to select the virtuous and capable. It is hoped that everyone can carefully select the virtuous and capable based on this intention. Representative of the Municipal Party Committee, Zhu Jiarang, stated that he was representing the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee to participate in the second election meeting of the Municipal Boy Scout Council. Recalling the first election meeting held at the Municipal Party Committee on October 5 last year, the organization of the Council had not yet been established, and the Shanghai Boy Scout cause had not yet been systematically developed. The command organization had not been formally established, and everything else could not proceed step by step on the right track. At that time, due to ideological differences, there were unfortunate misunderstandings, and the spirit of true unity could not be achieved, making the entire glorious and sacred Boy Scout cause appear bleak. At that time, the Municipal Party Committee, under the orders of the Central Committee and the entrustment of the China Boy Scout Headquarters, overcame all difficulties and made every effort to rectify the situation. After repeated discussions and clarifications, they were advised to cultivate morality and pursue perfection. On the one hand, they tried to eliminate all the wrong views in the Boy Scout community to create a harmonious atmosphere. On the other hand, they actively prepared to organize the Council to provide the Shanghai Boy Scouts with a central and unified command organization. All the Boy Scouts' efforts would have a center and a destination. Based on this principle, the Council's organizational regulations promulgated by the Headquarters were followed on October 5 last year, and the Municipal Party Committee convened city-wide service personnel to elect the first Council, which was officially established as the Shanghai Municipal Boy Scout Council of China. To this day, eleven months have passed, and the second election is being held today, and the second Council will be produced. This shows that all comrades in the city's Boy Scout community can make joint efforts based on the foundation of the past rectification by the Party Committee. They have corrected all the past negative phenomena and created today's atmosphere of one mind and one heart, sincerity and unity, and prosperity. This is what I am determined to do today after participating in this meeting and recalling the past eleven months. The extension of the Council's election is due to factual reasons, and it is being held today. The past work should be reported to the public by the Council, and we should conduct a rigorous inspection and criticism based on its work progress. At the same time, we can also point out its direction. We must know that the reason why the Boy Scouts are not directly commanded by the Party Committee but are subordinate to the Council is because the Party respects the Boy Scout cause. Because the Boy Scout cause is specialized knowledge, it must be directly led by an organization like the Council. The Party is only responsible for supervision and guidance. Therefore, the quality of the Council's work and the virtue and ability of the council members should be examined and selected by all the service personnel themselves. Today's meeting has such an important mission. All our service personnel comrades should understand and pay serious attention to this. As for today's election of council members, it is closely related to the rise and fall of the city's Boy Scout cause in the future. Everyone should stand firm, hold firm to their intentions, and take the two words "virtue" and "ability" as the sole standard. Focus on the four words printed on the ballot (select the virtuous and capable). Our first condition is naturally the word "virtue." If the individual has indeed excellent scholarship, high morality, and a deep understanding of Party principles and Boy Scout discipline, then we can elect him. Secondly, we must ask whether this person, though virtuous, is capable. Because being a Boy Scout council member requires practical work. If the individual has excellent talent but lacks ability, or if he has ability but cannot work in the Council due to being busy or other reasons, then we should not elect this person. There is also the kind of person who has a long history but only has a false reputation, who is unwilling to work or is incompatible with emotions, does not abide by discipline, and is good at manipulating people. We should not elect him either, because this kind of person cannot do practical work for the Council and may even disrupt things. You yourselves know how to choose your future leaders. The Party's hope and the will of the masses are probably the same as your original ideas. Finally, we wish that today five truly popular and well-deserved council members can be produced to move the Boy Scout cause in Shanghai a big step forward on the road of progress. The great torch will shine all over China and the world. Done. Representative of the Municipal Government, Chen Kecheng, said that he was very happy to represent the Municipal Government at the meeting. The Municipal Government attaches great importance to the Boy Scout cause. The initial financial assistance is proof of this. The Boy Scouts are not only a public cause but also a national cause. Because it is a national cause, it should not only be internal but also external. I believe everyone understands this. The Municipal Government places the Boy Scouts in the education cause and is managed by the Education Bureau, which should have a development plan. In the past, the Municipal Government believed that the most satisfactory thing in everyone's efforts was that everyone could unite and jointly develop the Boy Scout cause. However, there is still a long way to go, and we must continue to work hard. It is hoped that today's election results will continue this spirit and make the Boy Scout cause thrive. As for the election standards, the representatives of the Headquarters and the Municipal Party Committee have already said that it is the two words "virtue" and "ability." "Virtue" means doing things for everyone instead of for oneself. "Ability" means being capable and doing things correctly. It is hoped that the next Council will work harder. Representative of the Municipal Education Bureau, Zhou Shang, said that the most dangerous thing in the world is the absence of virtue and ability. Therefore, in today's election, we must pay special attention to the two words "virtue" and "ability." Secondly, we must also pay attention to the Boy Scouts' own goals. We must pay attention to the path we are taking, which is to save people. We must first be able to save ourselves before we can go and save others. In this regard, we should pay special attention to our own cultivation and training.

▲ Election Results: Wang Gang 72 votes, Gu Zhengli 52 votes, Leng Xueqiao 33 votes, Qu Yue 29 votes, Xu Zicheng 26 votes. The above five people were elected as council members. The next most votes: Zhang Xunfang 24 votes, Yu Kuikui 23 votes, Zhao Weizu 19 votes. The above three people were elected as alternate council members. The election ballots were checked and found to be correct, and the representative of the Headquarters and the chairman sealed and signed them together, and the report will be submitted to the Headquarters for record.

Han Wenxin and Sun Ti Return to China After Completing Their Studies 148

Mr. Han Wenxin is from Tianjin, Hebei Province. He graduated from Yenching University in 1918 with a Bachelor of Arts degree. After graduation, recognizing the lack of dentists in China, he entered the Peiping Dental School to specialize in dentistry. After graduating, he practiced medicine in the two major hospitals in Peiping, Union and Xiehe, for many years. In 1928, he studied abroad at his own expense in the University of California, School of Dentistry, specializing in dental medicine for several years. After obtaining a Doctor of Dental Surgery degree from the university, he was retained by the school to teach dental pathology for half a year. During his teaching, he also translated many famous dental medical books. He recently returned to China, bringing with him more than 500 pieces of dental equipment and more than 100 self-made new denture models. After returning to China, he was earnestly persuaded by Liu Ruiheng, the director of the Nanjing Central Hospital, to stay in Beijing and serve as the director of the dental department, in order to create a special dental department in the hospital. He is currently staying in Shanghai to purchase various necessary medicines and will go to Nanjing to take office in a few days. He plans to open a formal dental school in Nanjing next year to train dental specialists for our country.

Mr. Han Wenxin

Mr. Sun Ti is from Wuxi, Jiangsu Province. He graduated from Shanghai Daxia University in 1928. After graduating, he studied in the United States at his own expense, entering New York University to study business administration, specializing in accounting. He studied in the United States for three years and has now returned to China and been hired as a professor at Shanghai University. In addition, he plans to use his spare time to take charge of accounting affairs for China Aviation Corporation.

Minutes of the Nanyang Advanced Commercial School Faculty Meeting 149

The day before yesterday (the 5th) afternoon, Wu Xinglian, the principal of Nanyang Advanced Commercial School, hosted a banquet for all the faculty members at the school, with 44 people attending. Hong Kong is Preparing to Participate in the Shanghai-Hong Kong Tennis Interport 157

Expected to Arrive in Shanghai on October 1

At the beginning of this tennis season, the Shanghai Tennis Association invited tennis associations from Hong Kong and Tianjin to Shanghai for an interport competition. However, the Tianjin Association lacked travel expenses, so their team was unable to attend. The Hong Kong Association is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the Hoover on October 1. The association has selected ten outstanding male and female players, whose names have not yet been announced. However, it is certain that both Da Qiong and Xiao Qiong will be coming. Shanghai has a wealth of talented Chinese and foreign male and female tennis players, and Lin Baohua, Qiu Feihai, Hyoteki, Theodore, Badkar, Canavaro, and others are among those selected. At that time, the competition will be fierce and will surely cause a sensation in Shanghai. The Hong Kong players will arrive in Shanghai on the 1st, and the competition will begin on the 2nd, lasting for three days and ending on the 5th. They will return to Hong Kong on the President Madison on the 6th. The Shanghai-Hong Kong Tennis Interport began in 1922, was suspended in 1924, and was revived in 1928. It has been held four times, and the two sides have won twice each.

▲ The bid gold fell back 11 taels and 8 mace, and the volatility was still quite large, with unpredictable ups and downs of 4 or 5 taels to 7 or 8 taels per day. This was because overseas news was complicated, and both long and short positions had mutual restraints, but people were still hesitant. At the beginning of the week, it was outside 780 taels, and then it hovered uncertainly. On Thursday morning, it reached 85 taels and 8 qian, and then it showed a potential decline. On Saturday, it suddenly became 70 taels and 02 qian. The total difference in this week was 15 taels and 6 qian. Compared with the previous few weeks, it fell back 11 taels and 8 qian. The silver market was slightly shrinking, and the Shanghai exchange rate did not rise or fall, but the internal situation seemed loose. However, hedging was not smooth, so there were very few transactions. Silent News of Sunday's Interest Spread 164

Yesterday was Sunday, and banks were closed as usual. The money market was desolate due to continuous rain, and there were few people. The result was also very quiet. The foreign interest spread price in the early market was 7 qian, 2 fen, 5 li, 2 hao and a half, and in the afternoon market it was 7 qian, 2 fen, 5 li, 3 hao and 7 a half. The difference was only 1 hao and 2 a half. The silver spread in the early market was 1 qian, and in the afternoon market it only opened at 5 fen. The situation was loose and then tight, showing the difficulty of turning around the silver market. The transaction volume in the early market was 235,000 yuan, and in the afternoon market it was 400,500 yuan. There were no transactions in banknotes in both markets. The money shops received and settled more than 5.4 million yuan in foreign public bills, and more than 38 million yuan in silver public bills. The remittances from various routes were more than 400,000 yuan, and the transactions of small money shops were more than 300,000 yuan. In the subsidiary currency market, the price of both the Jiangnan small foreign currency and the Shanghai small foreign currency was 6 qian, 5 fen, and 9 li. The transaction volume in the early market was 3,500 jiao, and in the afternoon market it was 2,000 jiao. The price of the Guangdong small foreign currency in the early market was 6 qian, 5 fen, 1 li, 7 hao and a half. After a long competition in the afternoon market, the result was the same as in the early market. The transaction volume in the early market was 85,000 jiao, and in the afternoon market it was only 15,000 jiao. The price of copper coins increased by 500 wen, to 371,000 wen.

20 Customs Bonds Also Fell 1 Yuan and 45

The market conditions of various bonds in the securities market in Shanghai last week: spot transactions were even more scarce than before, with only 14,000 yuan traded in a week. Futures were more active than the previous week, and the market sentiment was very lively. The inflow and outflow of important bonds were very active. Even the newly auctioned salt tax treasury bonds gradually occupied a position in the market. The futures for this and next month have all been opened. The daily transaction volume was relatively clear only on Monday, with a total of 6.1 million yuan traded. Afterwards, the daily volume was quite good, with 10 million yuan on Tuesday and 17 to 18 million yuan on Wednesday and Thursday. The weekend volume was about 15 million yuan. The total volume for the week was 81.39 million yuan, an increase of 29.3 million yuan compared to the previous week. The unified tax bonds were still the most active, accounting for 30.345 million yuan, with 22.865 million yuan for the September contract and 7.48 million yuan for the October contract. As for the trend of various bonds, although the situation in the north has calmed down, the national disasters are extremely large. Although there was news of peace in Guangdong before, there has been no further development. In addition, the national treasury needs a large amount of money, and new bonds continue to be issued. All of these are enough to weaken the market sentiment, and the issuance of new bonds especially affects the market's supply and demand. Therefore, the bond market situation last week was worse than before. Large households were cautious and did not dare to make large-scale purchases. The buying sentiment was always dominant in the market. In the first two days of the week, although the prices hovered downward, the fluctuations were extremely small. On Wednesday, due to some selling, the demand and supply were very different, and the prices fell sharply. Although it rebounded on Thursday, the prices of unified tax and salt tax bonds were still low. In the last few days of the week, the market was in a chaotic state, with very small fluctuations. Free Talk

Not Removing the Garden Grass, Zhaifu's Anecdotes

The Big Fat Man 182

Last year, a big fat man came to the New World. His name was Jolly Ray. He weighed more than five hundred and sixty pounds, three and a half times my weight. So I cut out his photo and wrote a playful poem, sending it to a small school for Chinese and arithmetic practice. My playful poem is:

(Jolly woman, fat within fat: Weighs five hundred and sixty pounds. Compare her to me, three and a half!)

This poem and photo were sent with a letter. In the letter, I hoped that the children would weigh themselves, calculate, and compare themselves with Ms. Jolly, changing the fourth line and sending it back to me. Then, I would have something to send them next time.

Undermining the Stage 183

A certain university professor likes to show off and holds many part-time positions, earning more than a thousand yuan per month. But after securing the positions, his energy couldn't keep up, leading to a complete mess. As a result, one of his jobs was terminated. My friend took over the position, performing his duties loyally and without avoiding hard work. The professor was very unhappy and repeatedly caused trouble in secret. My friend told me everything, so I wrote a portrait for this professor. This professor is truly representative. People like him can be found everywhere in society. In a diligent society, lazy people are not allowed to linger; in a lazy society, diligent people are not allowed to establish themselves. What kind of society is China?

(Loves to play leading roles in plays; but lazy to take responsibility after getting the role. When others perform a good play, they secretly tear down the stage.)

Japanese Commerce in Qingdao 184

— Nangong Sheng

Recently, the Wanbaoshan incident has not yet been resolved. The Qingdao National Essence Society is also picking quarrels with Chinese people. The ambition of the Japanese is evident here. The Japanese operate with great effort in Qingdao, treating it as a colony. Therefore, newspapers run by the Japanese have absurd discussions of re-leasing Qingdao to Japan. Chinese people should pay attention to this and curb their ambition.

Qingdao was initially leased to Germany. The Japanese took it for themselves during the European War. Later, they were forced by the Washington Conference to reluctantly return it to our country. However, the rights to the Jiaoji Railway are still in the hands of the Japanese. The essence of the entire port has also been moved elsewhere by the Japanese. After the Japanese defeated the German army and seized power, it took several years to return it to our country. During those years, more than one hundred thousand Japanese moved to Qingdao. All businesses are controlled by the Japanese. The number of shops is unmatched by any other place. If you stand on the high ground of the island and look around, you only see short houses like combs, and the sound of wooden clogs is everywhere. These are all houses built by the Japanese.

The businesses run by the Japanese are comprehensive, including theaters and brothels. The most prosperous areas of Qingdao are Shandong Road (now renamed Zhongshan Road) and Sifang Road, with Shandong Road being the most important. Most of the shops are run by the Japanese. Confectioneries, clothing stores, restaurants, etc., are everywhere. Japanese shop signs are everywhere. Approximately every ten zhang, you can see a shop set up by the Japanese. The Japanese in Qingdao buy everything at shops set up by the Japanese. Therefore, business is very prosperous. This also shows the patriotic spirit of the Japanese. The Chinese people are far from being their match. Outside Shandong Road, there is also the so-called Japanese Quarter, southwest of Dabaodao. All the houses are Japanese-style. All the shops are set up by the Japanese. There are many restaurants, information centers, brothels, and coffee shops. The shop assistants employed in the shops are also Japanese women. Looking around, it's as if you have entered Japanese territory. It is appropriate for the Japanese to regard it as a colony.

The Qingdao vegetable market is gathered at the small vegetable market. The vegetable shops set up by the Japanese are in a ratio of two to one compared to the Chinese. The market is divided into three floors. The first and second floors are half Chinese and half Japanese. The third floor is entirely Japanese shops, selling toys. Many Chinese buy them. It is said that thirty thousand yuan leaks out in a year. From this, we can see the invasion of the Japanese. Even something as small as a toy is so huge. Shouldn't we be afraid?

When the Japanese held power in Qingdao, they planted their national flower, the cherry blossom, all over the island. In the First Park, the Shinto shrine, and the other five parks, tens of thousands of cherry trees were planted. Every year in February and March, the snow-white blossoms are magnificent. The Japanese still promote the Cherry Blossom Festival. At that time, all the Japanese in the city are crazy and ecstatic, as if they are in their own country. Stalls are set up everywhere, creating another large business area for the Japanese.

Japanese commerce in Qingdao can be described as meticulous. Even pawnshops are capitalized by the Japanese. Because the Chinese people are afraid of the power of the military, they dare not set up pawnshops. The Japanese take their place. The interest rates are unparalleled, reaching seven points per yuan. The poor people have no choice but to drink poison to quench their thirst, painfully going to pawn their belongings. Moreover, the deadline is only two months. As a result, the Japanese accumulate profits, all from the blood and sweat of the Chinese people.

The Invention of Talking Love Letters 185

— Ming

Recently, the progress of science in Western countries is astonishing. And recently in the United States, there has been the invention of talking letters. The so-called talking letters can transmit both images and sound. Young men and women are using them to send love letters. This matter caused a sensation, and it is especially lively in New York City. The person sending the letter enters a small room and speaks into a microphone. A short letter takes only one and a half minutes. If the letter is longer, the time is extended accordingly. When speaking, the green light comes on first, then the white light, indicating that the time is almost up, with only twenty seconds remaining. Stop talking when you see the red light. As for the recorded language, it is engraved into lines with a diamond to transmit the image. Currently, there are six institutions in New York City that provide this service. The number of people sending letters is increasing daily. In addition to young men and women using it to send love letters, other sectors, such as merchants ordering goods and pastors preaching, also use it to transmit or report messages in emergencies. It is incredibly convenient. However, this kind of machine has not been invented for long, and if the person sending the letter is not familiar with science, it is inconvenient to send it. Therefore, it is not yet widespread.

Traces of the Iron Ox 186

— Chezun

I once served in the Huaiyang Military Headquarters. Whenever there was a task, I had to follow, enduring the hardships of travel. I almost covered the north and south banks of the Yangtze River and both sides of the Grand Canal. Mapeng Bay is about seven or eight li away from Qingshui Pool, with Tie Niu Bay (Iron Ox Bay) in between. I have visited that place several times and often lingered and gazed at it. The iron ox is shaped like a regular ox, with its four hooves bent and resting on the ground, its head raised to the right, as if looking at something. To the right of the Guan帝 Temple in Shaobo Town, there is also an iron ox, similar in appearance to the ox in Tie Niu Bay. Near Gaoliangjian on the edge of Hongze Lake, there are nine iron oxen, each about one or two li apart, commonly known as Jiu Niu Bay (Nine Ox Bay). My sister's husband, Mr. Deng, lives by the lake and is a member of the River Works Committee. Therefore, I had the opportunity to see the nine iron oxen in person. However, the meaning of their placement is unclear. When I asked the local people, some said that the iron ox was to drive away monsters. In the past, when Xu Zhenjun pursued and captured water monsters, he rode a divine ox. When the monster saw Zhenjun, it was terrified and ran away. Seeing an ox lying on the embankment, it assumed Zhenjun was there and dared not stop running. Others said that the water could not pass over the ox's nose, which proved to be true. Every time you see oxen crossing a large river, their noses are raised out of the water. Casting oxen is a way to show the method of suppression. This is what is passed down. I don't know which is correct. According to my research, the Gaojia Weir was once breached by the Yuan people. At that time, it was planned to flood the area to ambush Zhu Taizu who was going to Lixiahe. The water went straight to Suzhou's Changmen. All the counties in Huaiyang became a vast ocean. Later, as the water gradually receded, the residents of Yanfu and Dongxing counties were all moved from Suzhou, planting grass as markers to divide the land for planting. When Zhu Ming established the dynasty and repaired the Gaojia Weir, Mr. Liu Qingtian surveyed the area and assessed the situation. All the iron oxen were cast by Qingtian and placed in selected locations. The meaning was undoubtedly to suppress flooding. This year's floods are so severe, unseen in a century. Whether the iron oxen can limit the effect of flooding is unknown.

Miscellaneous Notes from Japan 187

— Aiai, sent from Tokyo

Summer in Tokyo

A fiery sun blankets the boundless earth. This is the season of suffering for the poor, and the time for the leisure and vacation of the bourgeoisie. The words "summer retreat" seem to be a term exclusively for officials and wealthy merchants in our country. They take their beautiful concubines and charming wives, settle in Mogan Mountain and on the coast of Beidaihe, cooling down with ice, spending their days leisurely. Those farmers who are tanned like soy sauce ducks by the scorching sun, the brothers sweating in factories, and the soldiers fighting hard on the battlefield filled with gunfire, they have never even dreamed that there is another cool world in this hot summer.

In Japan, the situation is somewhat different. They are extremely egalitarian about beach vacations. Perhaps it can be said that summer retreats for the Japanese are a transformation of tightened living during the summer. Because areas near the sea are usually desolate, with a lower population density, and the cost of living is one-third cheaper than in the cities. Therefore, most of the city dwellers who have the possibility of moving spend two or three months on the coast during this long summer. On the one hand, they can exercise their body and mind through sea bathing, and on the other hand, they can reduce living expenses. Japanese families are the simplest. Their furnishings do not include heavy furniture such as tables, benches, wardrobes, and beds. So, when traveling, they can leave at any time. It is not difficult to take two or three boxes with them. When the autumn is cool and the wild geese return, they move back to the city. This back-and-forth movement has become a common habit for most people.

Those who cannot travel far due to their duties, aren't they too annoyed and overworked? For this reason, the social departments of major companies spend thousands of dollars to select scenic areas and establish summer cool-down gatherings for the entertainment of the general public. The streets are plastered with colorful advertisements with artistic colors. They are sincerely welcoming tourists. These organizations are purely voluntary in nature. Tourists who participate do not need to spend a penny.

The most wonderful summer cool-down gatherings this year are undoubtedly those of the Ueno Matsuzakaya. They have come up with a unique idea of turning the entire rooftop garden into a winter scene. The surroundings of the garden are equipped with animated scenery. The light gray sky is falling with goose-feather-sized snowflakes. The water in the small pond is frozen into thick ice. There are lions made of snow, and nude models of beautiful women sculpted from snow. Looking around, one sees jade towers and pavilions, all white. The little birds are chirping on the branches, playing the game of pecking snow. Young women, dressed in winter costumes, sing and dance in the nature covered with white velvet carpets, braving the cold and treading on the snow. Everything is decorated realistically, as if winter has really arrived. The garden has movies, dramas, dancing, and comical talks, and you can enter at will without admission tickets. In addition to Matsuzakaya, Sumida Park, Hibiya Park, Shiba Park, and Ryogoku Kokugikan also have summer cool-down gatherings. Either countless boats are prepared, allowing tourists to sway in the green waves, or Chaplin's comedies and the masterpieces of passionate girl Clara Bow are shown. Every evening when the sun sets, all places are crowded with tourists. Violinists play majestic and sorrowful music, and comedians win infinite laughter. Wonderful dances and light songs last until the night is quiet, and then they go home with satisfaction. It's just that those of us who are guests in Japan, looking at the joy of others, looking back at the displaced compatriots in our motherland, always feel that the sad people have different feelings in their hearts, which is extremely sad to say.

Records of What I Saw and Heard in the Old Capital 188

— Zhuan

Xiya

Nalan Rongruo's Luting Miscellaneous Records states that Li Wenzheng of the Ming Dynasty was granted a residence west of Xichang'anmen, commonly known as Li Gelao Alley. His villa was north of Bei'anmen. Bei'anmen is Diani'anmen, commonly known as the Back Gate. Outside the gate is Shichahai. From here, the Dan Tuo stretches to Jishuitan, where the Yuquan spring water enters the city and accumulates. During the heyday of the Yuan Dynasty, this water was west of the city. The southward-bound cargo ships entered the city through the Tonghui River and gathered in this pool. The tooth walls and brocade cables were crowded and bustling, almost like the story of Emperor Xuanzong's "Song of Obtaining Treasures." During the Ming Dynasty, the city walls were reduced, and cargo ships started warehouses in the east of the city. This place became smoky water, so that a corner of the imperial city could inspire the thought of thousands of miles of rivers and lakes. It is fitting that Wenzheng lingered here, creating a famous site. Wenzheng's Huai Lu Tang Ji has twelve poems of Xiya, Xiya is behind Ci'ensi Temple, and Duke Li took it as his title. This was Duke Li's ancestral home, not a villa. Rongruo made a mistake. The twelve poems are: 1. Hai Zi, 2. West Mountain, 3. Ci'ensi Temple, 4. Xiang Gate, 5. Drinking Horse Pond, 6. Yangliu Bay, 7. Bell and Drum Tower, 8. Ju Gao Pavilion, 9. Rice Field, 10. Peng Pond, 11. Vegetable Garden, 12. Guangfu Temple. They are all scenes from Jishuitan to Shichahai. During the Jiaqing era, Fa Wumen revisited the former residence of Xiya and asked Luo Liangfeng to paint a sequel to the Twelve Pictures of Xiya. For a time, famous people wrote poems and praises, and my uncle Huang Zaitong once copied a copy by hand. During the winter vacation of the Renyin year, I borrowed it from his house and copied several paintings. Huang's poem says, "Xiya was originally the Yuan Xihai, (Jishuitan printed Yuan Xihai Zi.) Wonderful paintings and clear chants several times each. (Xiya made a painting starting with Shen Shitian Wenhengshan. Wumen shikan has more than fifty paintings, and I have seen more than ten paintings. Many elders in the Jiaqing era wrote poems.) Laymen's shrines still have residences, and the Prime Minister's land originally lacked pavilions. (Xiya is Li Wenzheng's ancestral property. There was no villa at first. Therefore, Duke Li's poem has a sentence saying "The green field has no hall, but I am thinking of installing it." For details, see Wumen's Examination of Xiya.) The mountain color of the previous dynasty is still on the city, and the elegant style is gone to the edge of the water. Pine trees and quinoa light gradually become familiar, and flowers are scheduled to come together every time. I followed up with a poem: "The peaceful leisure people are like the meeting, the paintings are traced and copied, and the first is returned. Looking south, I like to sing Huai Lu Ji, and the east wind has lost the national flower platform. In the misty alleys and deserted smoke, the desolate gardens and forests are on the edge of the wild water. I am afraid that few people will come to read the epitaph on the suburban tomb of the virtuous ancients."

Wenzheng's tomb is in Weiwu Village outside Xizhimen, close to Jile Temple. The temple is famous for its crabapple blossoms and has a National Flower Terrace. Although the terrace is still there, the trees are desolate, and the name of the village has also been changed. During the spring of Guihai, I rode a donkey with Fang Yushan to visit. After asking around, I finally found the place. Therefore, there is a couplet at the end of this poem. Today, the Jishuitan area is empty and bright, with gulls, reeds, and the elegance of a marsh. The houses near the water often hear the sound of fulling blocks, especially separated from the times. The reclusive scholars of the old capital love to build huts here. Xu Su Yi of Wuxi built a house here, piling up stones by the stream and moving bamboo to become a barrier. Late in the summer, friends gathered, and the meaning was far away. I once used a sentence to describe the scene, "The willow trees are shaded with endless green, and the rain makes the distant mountains constantly blue." It is not as good as Song Muzhong's poem about passing the old residence on Yinding Bridge, which is especially skillful. Song's poem says, "The Drum Tower is connected to the back lake bay to the west, and the Yinding Bridge is horizontal between the sunsets. The endless blue waves are connected to Taiye, and the sunny green is still sent to the distant mountains. The pine and pagoda trees are still in the old courtyard, and the fairy music is leisurely over the years. The white-haired alchemist has been talking about tea for a long time, and the spring breeze is cold, and the crows are still returning."

From Jishuitan south to Shichahai, there are several acres of rice fields. In the city, this scene is especially strange. The Ju Gao is squeaking, just like in Jiangnan. A long embankment is covered with official willow trees. On both sides of the bank, there are reed sheds and ice carriers, bustling for a distance of about a mile. The Manchu men and women, with heavy makeup and flamboyant clothes, play among them. In recent years, the customs of the old capital have gradually changed. Only here can we still see the remnants of the Spring Bright Dream. On the north bank, there is a restaurant called Huixiantang, which is also purely old-fashioned. Overlooking the railing, the whole view is in sight. Holding a glass of wine, I think as if I am a person after the Southern Crossing thinking of the prosperity of Bianjing.

Jiang Hongjiao's novel "Husband's Wife" is suspended for one day.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Love Song Exchanges 189

— By Man Yin

Published by the Folklore Society, compiled by Qiu Jun

(In the minds of ordinary people, it is believed that only scholars with bellies full of ink can produce good literature. However, in my opinion, that is not entirely true. No matter how much ink they have drunk or how accomplished they are, there are things in their works that cannot be considered literature. Conversely, no matter how uncultured some people may be, they can still produce good literary works... ) This is what was said in an article introducing (Further Selections of White Snow Tunes) published in this journal last year. We certainly agree that it is correct. Originally, so-called literary works are produced by gradually refining and transforming genuine emotional folk songs and slang. We can compare the genuine and moving aspects of a work to a beautiful woman, and beautiful words and phrases to fine clothing. A beautiful woman is naturally even more beautiful in fine clothing, but not everyone in fine clothing is a beautiful woman. Similarly, neat formatting and ornate language do not necessarily make a good work. As long as genuine emotions are expressed and the meaning is sincere, even vulgar slang can be considered first-rate literature. Just look at the collections of folk love songs published in various countries around the world that have been passed down through the ages. The most notable example is the Book of Songs in our Five Classics, which is nothing more than folk songs and slang from the Zhou Dynasty. Confucius and other masters not only did not dismiss it, but instead worked hard to organize it.

Therefore, we really have no reason not to recognize folk love songs as literary works and not engage in research and exploration. Recently, to relieve the tedium of the long summer days, I borrowed a pile of folk literature books from the library and from friends, giving me the opportunity to appreciate the truth, beauty, and goodness of folk literature and fulfill my long-cherished wish. This is a very worthwhile and gratifying thing for me. After enjoying them, in addition to paying tribute to the editors of this series, I have specifically selected this book (Love Song Exchanges) to introduce to the readers of this journal for general appreciation.

This is a special collection of love songs exchanged between men and women in rural villages. At any time, in the mountains and fields, there are always many farmers who, when tired from work or during their leisure time, cannot help but sing mountain songs that leisurely linger and attract the opposite sex. This book contains these lyrics.

The entire book is divided into three volumes. The first volume (Nanyang Journey) (The story concerns men from Lingnan who are going to Nanyang. As they prepare to leave their homes and cross the ocean, the women feel sad. Thus, during their farewells, they each express their pain, and their sincere words become lyrics...) is divided into three sections with a total of one hundred songs. The second volume is a collection of common love songs exchanged between men and women, divided into sections such as "Expressing Feelings," "Her Ideal Lover," "Separation and Reunion," "Affectionate Words," "Words of Farewell," "The Amazing Same Name," "Questions," and "Jokes," with a total of one hundred songs. The third volume is also a collection of common love songs exchanged between men and women, divided into more than twenty sections such as "Hard to Part," "Eighteen Answers," "Love and Money," "Exclusive Love and Multiple Loves," "Old Man and Young Woman," "Scholar's Farewell to His Wife," "Searching Thousands of Miles for Unmarried Grandchildren," "A Glimpse of the Han River," "Keeping Secrets," "Exposure of Spring Light," "Questions," "Communication," "Gifts," "Marks of Marriage," "Love and Pain," "Following Footprints," "Farewell," and "Teasing," with a total of one hundred songs. Some of them have explanations in front, and there are national language annotations for those song phrases that are not easily understood by scholars. It not only preserves the original appearance of the folk songs, but also makes it clear at a glance. We cannot help but appreciate and praise the editor's hard work.

Since the entire volume consists of folk songs and, moreover, love songs, it is naturally inevitable that there will be vulgarity, or even obscenity. However, it is a genuine expression of emotion and a sincere attitude, and it can be asserted that they have no choice but to sing them. This alone, as mentioned earlier, is enough to qualify them as good literary works. Moreover, there are many phrases that are sonorous, meaningful, and use appropriate metaphors.

In addition, folk love songs contain a lot of valuable data for the study of history, language, anthropology, sociology... such as local customs, habits, and the psychology of the people. For example, in the second volume of this book ("Her Ideal Lover"), we can learn that rural women do not welcome scholars as their (black lacquered benches), but welcome rough farmers, which is exactly the opposite of the modern women who hope their lovers are doctors and masters. The reason is:

Do not marry a scholar,

Who leaves you alone all year round.

Better to marry a farmer,

With whom you can discuss things intimately.

Because they cannot resist the suffering of sexual frustration, they think of resolving it. There are also women who have tried to transgress moral principles, break the law, and disregard reputation and life and death, truly sacrificing themselves for love. For example, the heroines in the fifth part of the first volume ("Wife Big Husband Small") and the third volume ("Exposure of Spring Light") sing about this kind of situation.

There are also triangular love stories, such as the one in the third volume ("Exclusive Love and Change"). However, here he or she is very frankly telling the new lover in front of the old lover. Their attitude of loyalty, honesty, and lack of hypocrisy is much more admirable than the sneaky and secretive behavior of young people today.

In short, in addition to the value of the lyrics for appreciation, this book also gives us a lot of information about the social situation in areas such as Pingyuan, Guangdong. Recently, our nationalistic literature and art has occupied the entire Chinese literary world. The so-called nationalism is to promote the inherent lively, brave, and striving spirit of the Chinese nation, resist imperialism, and revitalize the national consciousness. Then, undoubtedly, we really need to pay attention to folk literature like this book, which vividly depicts the national character. This article concludes on this point and introduces this book to the public.
