Youth Corner

Lessons 190

— By A'mei

(1)

Standing at the entrance of the Mengyuan Hotel, watching Wanfen's figure disappear around the corner of Zhejiang Road, he thought that things were going too smoothly.

An hour ago, Wanfen gave him an opportunity to feel numb and excited. She said,

"Ah Lin, does that female classmate of yours still often look for you?"

"Why would she often look for me? I'm afraid she'd rather spend her time with her boyfriend."

"Aren't you her boyfriend?" Wanfen's words pierced his heart. Ah Lin blushed.

"Wanfen," Ah Lin took her hand, "Why do you say such things too? Don't you know my heart?"

"Hmph, you're too serious. Can't you tell I'm joking?"

"Wanfen, this only proves how deeply you love me. The meaning of your so-called joke contains the courage to protect me."

"The person I love most in the world is you, think about it, Ah Lin. If you ran away from me, my life would be over. How could I not watch over you all the time?"

Moved to the point of embracing this woman and giving her a long kiss was not enough to express his gratitude, Ah Lin shed tears.

"Ah Lin, has your money not been wired yet?"

"Oh, damn, I forgot all about it. Here, take it."

The woman took the money and said,

"How about we go to the Mingyuan tonight for some fun?"

Slightly hesitant, Wanfen understood what he meant.

"If you don't have time today, tomorrow at the Yuegong would be fine too."

"Eleven o'clock then, you wait for me. Really, I've been wanting to dance these past few days."

Reluctantly, they said goodbye.

(2)

"I thought you went out. You're too late. Is there any mail from home?"

Yizhen opened the door and blurted out.

"Hey, the people at home are really hopeless. I really wonder why parents can't understand their children's hearts. They said they absolutely cannot dissolve the engagement."

"Then how are you going to resolve it?"

"I'll break off relations with my family."

"But there's a financial problem. Even if you don't study anymore, finding a job won't be easy."

Ah Lin didn't answer. The woman continued, "What about the two books you promised me?"

"Oh, I'm sorry, but it's also because my family hasn't sent any money."

Ah Lin was very surprised, but the woman had already picked up the handkerchief from the table. The two words "Wanfen" embroidered on the corner of the handkerchief made Yizhen understand her lover's recent behavior. She didn't say anything.

"I was going to give it to you," Ah Lin said.

"Then forgive me for not thanking you."

After the woman said this, she wanted to leave. The man was perfunctorily trying to keep her.

"You're just nagging, do you think me staying here with you means I love you?"

"Then, goodbye."

"Goodbye."

Yizhen left. Ah Lin celebrated his own skill in handling things.

(3)

The streets were crowded and noisy. Streetcars rolled on the asphalt roads. The red and green lights of the shops seemed to smile at everyone. Graceful women pressed onto the sidewalks, captivating the souls of ambitious men.

With a cigar in his mouth, no one could say that this young man wasn't happy. The rickshaw stopped on the side of North Sichuan Road. Ah Lin walked into the Yuegong.

In the dim light, he couldn't find Wanfen. The dance floor was filled with five-colored flesh. People were intoxicated. Dance, dance, dance until they were tired. He vaguely saw a woman who looked like Wanfen walking towards him. He went to the back and indeed knew it was Wanfen. He stood up, his anxiety completely gone at this time, preparing to greet the woman with a welcoming expression. He called out,

"Wanfen!"

But Wanfen ignored him, glanced at him proudly, and threw herself into a man's arms and sat down.

How should he resolve this awkward situation? A man's self-esteem made Ah Lin feel that arguing with that woman now would be no different from inviting humiliation. He only thought about how he had wronged Yizhen.

Thinking in the gentle night breeze, the contented people walking under the streetlights no longer included Ah Lin.

(4)

Two letters were on the desk. He knew that the letter from home was urging him to get married, and Yizhen's letter was undoubtedly asking him to join some research society.

But after reading the letters, he fainted on the bed. Everything was over. His family said that since he was able to choose his own marriage, he should naturally be able to support a woman, so they could no longer send him money. But why were Yizhen's words so firm? She said,

"... A love with cracks, let it break. Ah Lin, I have already decided to dedicate my heart to someone else..."

Crying and laughing were useless. The situation was beyond remedy in every aspect. Only the shadow of the word "lessons" danced before Ah Lin's eyes.

(2) Books should be limited to those concerning youth issues.

(3) Photos related to youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, theater, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are welcome, whether individual or group. Please do not write on both sides of the paper.

Social News

Marshal Foch's Diary of the European War 192

— Translated by Gu Angruo

I congratulated General Pershing. On September 13, 14, and 15, our troops tightly defended the new positions recaptured from the enemy.

The American First Army must now transfer most of its troops to the west of the Meuse River to show its great strength.

Having previously decided on September 2 that the American army would attack Saint-Mihiel on September 3, I now order the three commanders-in-chief of the British, French, and American armies to advance towards the Cambrai-Saint-Quentin-Mézières line. The German transverse railway is within reach. The American army will launch a fierce attack west of the Meuse River.

The Allied offensive from the Seille River to the Aisne River is now developing smoothly. The enemy army began a full retreat. All Allied forces were then divided and brought together to attack, and the offensive routes are as follows:

(1) The British army, with the French army covering its left flank, will continue to advance towards Cambrai and Saint-Quentin.

(2) The central units of the French army will drive the enemy back across the Aisne River and the Ailette River.

(3) The American army (A) will operate in the Woëvre area, with the goal of clearing the Paris-Avricourt railway line and obtaining a base of operations for the next attack. This battle must take place no later than September 10 to prevent the enemy from taking the opportunity to replenish its strength. (B) On the east side, with the Meuse River covering its left flank and with the French Fourth Army supporting it, it will launch a fierce attack towards Mézières. This battle must take place no later than between September 20 and 25. The first goal is to fight on both sides of the Argonne Forest and defeat the enemy to the Stenay-Lessives-Attigny line. The second goal is to occupy Mézières and advance eastward to take the Aisne River.

I do not give up my plan for the British army to directly attack the Hindenburg Line. On September 8, I wrote to Field Marshal Haig, asking him to (immediately begin preparations to conquer this defense line, and to advance beyond this line to the designated destination. If you want to attack the enemy by surprise, then this attack should not be delayed).

The next day, September 9, I went to La Panne to meet with King Albert of Belgium, and explained to him that now that the German army is wavering and its forces are mostly concentrated in France, our army can take the opportunity to drive back the enemy forces in Belgium and recover the lost territories north of the Yser River. We then further discussed the battle plan, instructing the British and French armies to cover the Belgian army's attack.

King Albert of Belgium fully agreed with this. I then went to Cassel to meet with Field Marshal Haig, General Dellemer, and Major General Gillain to discuss in detail and immediately draft a battle plan.

The first step is to prepare a base of operations for the offensive, with the goal of occupying the Kemmelberg ridge, the Holset Forest, the Bainghemberg ridge, Scherpenheuvel, the Vloka Ridge, Langemark, Woumen, and the Comines Canal. The second step is to actively advance towards Bruges to clear the Belgian coast, and to attack towards Tielt and Ghent. The first battle will be fought by nine divisions of the Belgian army and two divisions of the British army. The second battle will be fought by most of the Belgian army, along with the British Second Army and three divisions of French infantry and three divisions of French cavalry.

After the meeting, I immediately issued a cover letter to the armies designated to participate in the operation, specifying the resolutions.

Commander-in-chief Pétain naturally did not remain uninformed of these plans, and I also notified him that, if necessary, I would like to appoint General Degoutte to take command.

On the morning of September 11, King Albert visited Panne, and I immediately asked him to command the Belgian army, and also designated the British and French forces participating in the operation to be under his command. He fully agreed, but requested that a formal military order be issued and that a French general be assigned as an assistant. General Degoutte was then appointed as the Chief of Staff of the Allied Army of Flanders, under the command of King Albert. Major General Gillain, Field Marshal Haig, and Commander-in-chief Pétain all received notification, but were firmly instructed to maintain strict secrecy on all aspects.

Field Marshal Haig fully agreed with my plan. On the 14th, he replied to my letter of September 8, stating that he was preparing to launch a fierce attack between Ypres and Comines in order to occupy the enemy defenses west of the Saint-Quentin Canal and the Scheldt River, and to allow the British Fourth Army to reach the position to attack the Hindenburg Line.

I ordered General Débeney to assist the right wing of the British Fourth Army with the left wing of the French First Army. This was his main and fixed operational task for the future. The military order stated, (Thereafter, the left wing of the French army must always cover the right wing of the British Fourth Army, and must always maintain contact between the two armies...).

On September 18, the British Fourth Army, with the protection of the left wing of the French First Army and the right wing of the British Third Army, successfully attacked the Holnon-Feuillaucourt-Hargicourt-Lempire-Épehy line. All designated goals were achieved. Over ten thousand prisoners were captured and one hundred and fifty cannons were seized. An especially important achievement was that our army had now advanced to the position to attack the Hindenburg Line. Furthermore, because Field Marshal Haig was preparing to direct the main attack on the Hindenburg Line from Saint-Quentin to Cambrai, the results of this battle were particularly important.

Field Marshal Haig immediately made arrangements with this goal in mind. On September 22, he ordered the British First, Third, and Fourth Armies to prepare for a general attack on the Hindenburg Line. Although he had not yet notified his subordinates of the date of the general attack, he had already decided in his heart to begin around the 25th.

The British Commander-in-Chief notified Commander-in-Chief Pétain of his plan and requested immediate reinforcements for the French First Army, especially in terms of artillery. Commander-in-Chief Pétain then drew reinforcements from the center of the Reserve Army Corps (because this route was not temporarily prepared for any important battles). The progress made in the past two months had shortened the Reserve Army Corps' battle line considerably, making it easy for Commander-in-Chief Pétain to draw reinforcements (To be continued).

Home
